Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear where the patients die now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse according to the divisions of treatments we have mentioned, and it does not profit, then you must apply three methods of cautery, all of which are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of these, one method is to make three or four cauteries in a line according to the length of the abscess, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have mentioned before.  
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	And do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient often turn onto their back. 
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	And another method of cautery is to heat the cautery that has two points, as we have shown in the case of shoulder dislocation. 
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	And lift the heart which is located near the abscess, or where the pain of the patient comes from the left, and let the elevation from which you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.  
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After he pierces the two inflamed nerves so that the heart is pierced from the other side, then draw out the cautery, and thus he will have four. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see, if you cauterize with the whole cautery at three nerves. 
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has festered for a long time, this is worth more than the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is of no use to someone with dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat it according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not profit, then it is necessary that you make him four cauteries around the shoulder, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the thigh, and two behind the back on the spine, and one at the breast.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	And let the cauteries be very close to the hope of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	Afterward leave the cautery uncovered for a long time to avoid putrefaction, and do not leave the patient after the cautery.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing would hasten, and the two intentions would be together with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the one we have shown before.  
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	And that for the back is oval-shaped, according to what has been put down before. 
de l’enfleure des piez	from the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical and are full of clear yellow fluid, it is fitting that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; 
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and apply your hand with the cautery without turning.  
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, so that you do not compress the yellow wax, and let the cautery be of this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	Afterwards, make two cauteries on each leg at the point of the knife; 
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; 
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauteries exposed for a long time without cleaning so that it can dry out. 
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the treatment of the other treatments that we have mentioned. 
de la menoison	From the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a stomach ailment comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retaining and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and it cannot be cured by ordinary remedies; 
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient suffering greatly and with much greening (bile), then make a large cautery on the stomach as has been spoken of before or a circling cautery of the stomach. 
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and four cauteries around the belly, subtle and all with a delicate point, and two cauteries on the thighs. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, burn them on the shoulder, and burn each one, and two small burns on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When hemorrhoids are at the fundament, one or several, and are old and composed of large, cold, and damp corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said by division, and it does no good, then make cauteries. 
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	III on the spine of the back, that which is all behind below the shoulder blade bit by bit in a triangular shape, and I cauterize below the elbow II twice. 
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	And if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then on the face we apply a large cautery to the stomach as it has been previously said, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with the whole cautery. 
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	And leave the cautery uncovered for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place until it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you apply an athlet, if it is heated so that it resembles a razor, and then put it all inflamed on the athlet applied; 
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	And leave it until your hand and the cautery reach the origin of the vein, so that the blood stops.  
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	Do this once or twice, and if there is much swelling, cauterize each one as we have said. 
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	After the treatment of wounds while they are healing. 
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	And if you cauterize with a large cautery on the wound, it will be of greater help. 
de plaie mal curee	from a poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer cutting or opening, which we will recount in their place, then comes a certain illness that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there comes a fistula, and it is old and has putrid and corrupting moisture, you must first test with a subtle probe and keep track of how deep the probe goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heating the cautery which resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the pus has entered, and repeat the cauterization until the dead and corrupted flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times according to the quantity needed. 
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	And beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins. 
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, beware of these places, and do not cauterize except in a fleshy place, and think that it is not a piercing. 
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After healing the place until it is healed, and if the pus is drained, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the place is entirely healed. 
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the materials are not removed, know that the place is infected and the bone rots at the base.  
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	And as one of these that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	of the sickness of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes as a result of great windiness and does not take any pleasure in women, then you must make a cautery on the reins on one side and the other with the small cautery that we have previously mentioned.
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	And if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line and they will make greater help. 
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the back part above the bladder where the pubic hair begins, on the right and left, and let each cautery be as long as the width of one thumb. 
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and make him do the cautery on his back, where you need it. 
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	And let the cautery be sharp according to the shape previously mentioned. 
de la marris	Of the sea
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the matrix is cold and moist, and does not allow conception because of this, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are delayed.
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, there is great pain:  
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	then it is necessary to make three cauteries around the vulva, as we have said in the bladder cautery, and two cauteries on his back.
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	And let the cauteries be sharp, as we have said. 
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When viscous moisture descends to the socket of the hip, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together. 
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	And when the place of the separation is found, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the bone of the hip with a cautery resembling a circle and mark in front of the place around the bone as it turns, so that the bone is within the circle. 
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	And let the cautery be such as that with which one cauterizes the stomach. 
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present to you, make three large cauteries from olive wood, and let the cautery be as perfect as all hearts.  
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure it until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes to the bone of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured by what we have said in the division and the cure is not worth it, and the illness is old: 
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	Then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills. 
Aprés li fai cautere;	After you do the cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	And the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: 
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	That is to say together burning medicines, and fire cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, of which some are such: 
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	That you cauterize upon the box of the hip three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make good depth and large ones, and there be between each cautery space the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; 
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Once done we make a cautery in the middle upon the head of the hip, so that there are four according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, if the cautery is applied with a circle as we have previously said for the dislocation of the hip; 
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	But do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire hip, and all the flesh around the core is burned. 
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done for sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it extends to the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle, four must be made on the left side with a dot. 
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	And the cauteries should be lancet-shaped, and the thickness of the flesh should be burned;  
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers or near the end of his foot, then cauterize him where he feels the pain three points or four with a cautery called "points". 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if necessary, do it again. 
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, do it with a knife cautery or a circular cautery, and be very careful in all your cauteries so that you do not leave the cautery long enough to burn the nerves and large arteries, and so that you do not cause the patient more pain and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have performed cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they let it be until the leg was all swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purge of the stomach from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery in one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the surgeons say about the cautery of the hip, which is the manner, make a tool and let its head be as thick as a doctor's nail or a little less, and let it have between the crosspieces and from one crosspiece to another the space of the size of a fingernail. 
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	And let the crosspieces be opposite in two parts and also like knots, and it has a well-made iron handle. 
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	Let it be warmed until it is all red and gives off sparks, and then put it on the affected hip bone, and turn it on the healthy side. 
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	And let the cautery burn once, when the cautery is hot, and leave it for three days. 
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	Then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time.
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment with anointing until it is healed.  
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	 Albucasim says that we use this cautery very little because of the fear of its appearance, and we rarely see anyone using it. 
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	And nevertheless, this is a good cautery for those who can endure it, and where it is applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The burning medicine cautery is such that you make an instrument with crossbars where the edge of the door descends, and it is made of iron or steel with a long side, and at the height it has two notches, and between each one there is the thickness of a finger. 
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and let them be opened by fire above, and join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	Then place the box on the hip of the patient lying on his sound side, and press your hand firmly on the box of the hip; 
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then put between the two circles of the hot awl that has been heated in the fire for a moment, and leave it there for an hour or so, allowing the patient to suffer the heat and burning. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For there will be as much biting pain as from fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the biting pain has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and remove the hip awl gently, and leave it like this for three days, applying butter until that part which is blackened by the burning is removed; 
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and let it stand for three days so that putrefaction sets in;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this would be the last aid after the treatment of wounds so long as they are healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make the instrument that you have made for the hip in the same way. 
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And this is the manner of the hot awl, and I have written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot coals, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	Where there is a small hole so that the point of a razor can enter.
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	And put one pot over the other well-sealed, and put alkali and lime and gentle heat on top, so that there are two above the powders until you have heated it well in your hand. 
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	And leave it like that until hot water and steam descend into the sealed pot, then take all that water and pour it over lime and alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered for many medical works and for other members' cauteries. 
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it makes a work like fire, and with other medicines that we cauterize well the hip like turpentine and honey of Anacardium and chalk with soap, all these things mixed together. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us of a remedy by which a man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic vein, and praised it greatly, and said that no other remedy was done, and that he was healed at once when this remedy was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches here after.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And say in a part manner that you take some green and fresh litharge, and grind it very much with a bit of fat, and put on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain holds, and bind it. 
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And leave it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning. 
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let it enter a bath so that its body is a little warmed up, and let it enter a bed, and the pain will go away entirely and it will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a fire cautery for such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of humors.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat hairs, it helps a lot. 
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and it must be done in a part manner. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow between the thumb and the other finger which is called the knuckle.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After you take goat's horn, and put it to fire until it is charcoal, and place it on wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. 
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	And do it again in the same way, and do not stop doing so until you think by sense that it reaches up to the hip, and that the pain has ceased. 
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	And this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat". 
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or from percussion or by too great an evacuation, or by similar cold matter spread out, none of these cases are worth cautery except for that which comes from infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is fitting after this that the patient is purged with fetid pills or other such things, which are made on his back, where the pain resides, three lines marked by an inch, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can suffer; 
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and it should be made as a cautery which is called "points".  
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see, make III or IV cauteries with a medium-sized cautery iron according to this form: 
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	This illness often comes upon small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight throat when they rise, and fear; 
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you will find in the last spine of the back, and in us the appearance that comes upon the other spines. 
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you are about to treat it, cauterize with a hot iron according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery brands each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, if you cauterize around the spine with a hot iron two or three lines, and the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After healing the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply the cautery in a gibbosity which is in the spasm of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When joint pains are from moist humors that are spread throughout each limb of the body, and when pain comes to the foot, which physicians properly call "gout," and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this way: 
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-sized according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need for you to grip on the face of the foot, make the burn with all the heat that one calls "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come to the knees and other joints, which happens many times, then make three or four cauteries on each knee from each part, with all olive oil cauteries. 
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand too strong except until the thickness of a grain of wheat is burned.  
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and the back, administer to him the cautery that we have mentioned in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, make dots around the wrist two lines long; 
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there is still pain in the arms, make dots on each joint and on the hair of the hand.  
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good treatment to the patient and take medicine.  
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give it good treatment and purge phlegm, it will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the facial bone
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture comes in the groin, and the bowels descend to the buttocks and it is new, then you must, when you see him healed, that he does not eat that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and let him use things that loosen the belly so that the fevers descend from his belly. 
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after you make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath while the bowels are repaired, and reset them at your will, and place a sign below the break on the bone where the dagger went in, and at any mark that resembles half of a circle above the body; 
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heat the cautery which has this shape:  
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and drips clear fluid.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bowels in their place; 
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and have the assistant hold his hand so they do not return backwards; 
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and work well on the patient's thighs, and put a cushion and a sergeant under his thighs, and another under his armpit which holds his hands; 
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	Then place the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone; and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you get to the bone. 
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	And be careful that the boil does not burst when you apply the cautery. 
que tu ne le brulasses;	That you do not burn it. 
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	And so that the patient does not die or suffer other ills. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to their size, and for adults also large according to their size;  
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	After three days, treat the area around the cautery with butter until the burn is gone. 
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	After that treatment with other ointments until it is healed, and have the patient lie on their back for forty days until the wound is well closed. 
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that his nourishments be left long, so that the eyeball does not protrude when he will go to the chambers. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he will want to rise, let him be given a well-made bandage and wear it for forty other days. 
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	And he should have good rest, work little, and beware of too much drinking and eating, and of shouting too loudly. 
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the treatment of the tailbone in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When tumors come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow any more, make a cautery with a cautery according to its quantity, and burn a third of the core.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	After the cure according to what we have said; 
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	And none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize it with a three-angled cautery according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first sign the place of the incision and make a line across its width above the fracture, and another behind it, and hold your hand steady over the whole cautery iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, whether from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help it, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called "points", and the cautery should be done according to the length of the limb, its smallness, weakness, and its virtue, and its location of twists and turns and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If he is healed by the first cautery, it is good; 
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If not, begin another cautery on top of it, for this custom is that it must change to the member which is closest, for which it is necessary that you make the cauteries until the patient is healed. 
de meselerie	from the art of surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The mesail are helped sometimes by cautery with great help, and the same disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	When you see it cauterized, be careful if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread nor remain, and you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: 
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	One in the middle of the head, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair;  
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape. 
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and let your hand remain there so that the cautery reaches the bone and so that the scabs come out, so that the vapors of the thick humors can be released; 
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize on the spot according to what is in front.  
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the inflammation is spread everywhere; 
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it is clearly wasting away, then you should cauterize with the cauteries that we have mentioned above, and one cautery on the top of the neck, and two on the spine of the back, and six on the spine of the back and one large one on the rump and another below, and two on the two shoulders; 
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and in the hollows of the hands; 
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and guard against the nerves that are on the back of the calf, so that you do not burn them; 
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never apply the cautery on the bone where the dagger struck, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that when you do more cauterizing, you do more good, and increase the benefit;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and know that the sick do not feel pain from the cautery as the healthy feel it, because the body is already all corrupted.  
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in a manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing, wash the wound with flour of beans mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes in a limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then apply cautery on the limb according to the size of the limb; 
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cauteries be a small puncture entering the thickness of the flesh;  
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And sometimes one does cautery to the hand and foot and back, at the point where the nerve that moves the limb emerges, and thus the swelling is removed. 
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And in all ways let no one interfere unless they are knowledgeable of the limbs and the origins of the nerves that move the body. 
de albaras	From aloes
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the illness called “albaras” is chronic, and medicine has no effect, then cauterize a spot with a cautery iron, according to the quantity of the species of the heart, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed.  
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	Then cure with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a dove and blood of an almond, of each one part. 
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be mixed all together, and let it be bound with a cloth, and let it air in place until it is healed. 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre first appears, and you see it stop growing, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And nevertheless the wise say that one should also apply cautery to the middle of the ulcer; 
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and nevertheless it does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen several times; 
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and more rightly the thing is that it should be cauterized around, with a cautery called "circular", as we have said in speaking of types of cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot move
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has an illness that is called "adubelati," and it lingers due to the excess that it causes or due to the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old), and he has little blood, or due to time; 
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see it hastening to die 
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then let the cautery burn around with many small burns, pricking. 
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards leave it thus. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce all the way through with the cautery, heat the cautery as follows.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness which is called "adubelati" as long as the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it behind in such a way that the course of the decay is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of illness there is which is called "corrodent", and it is nothing else but a devouring of a limb, for it gnaws the limbs as fire gnaws dry twigs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this illness in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries very small and large, according to what suits the place where the illness is; 
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	afterwards cauterize from all sides until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted is removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and apply a cauterized poultice softened with oil to the burns so that the burning sores are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of wounds generating flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, that's good;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, start the cautery again on what remains of the corrupted flesh. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this condition has sometimes been cured with medicinal water in place of fire cautery;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	But nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for the malady of fever in the division. 
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the purples that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that by fire comes a disease which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large foul thing which bleeds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know the fire cautery, and the hot iron cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery point as thin as a goose feather, and it should be made of good iron to the size that it can pierce nails from all sides, and that it has subtle edges. 
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	Afterwards, you put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail.  
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	And leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot. 
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make a plaster of wild mallows ground with salt and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. 
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place of the wound by anointing with fat until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by fire the body, and it often happens in hands and feet, then you must administer a hot cautery to them. 
et est en teil maniere:	And it is in this manner: 
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a cane of iron or a feather of vulture, and put it on the nail and the surrounding skin, that is to say for warts. 
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And put the cane on it so that it encompasses everything around, then put a piece of hot coal on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and can find the way of the hot coal deep down to the root;  
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient endure the bite of the hot coal for an hour. 
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Then leave it like that, and it will come out by the roots.  
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do one after another, until you have removed all those that are on the body, then treat the wounds which generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When someone trembles from coldness of nerves, or from quartan fever or another, it is fitting that you make them four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine. 
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	And one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach with olive oil cautery; 
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	This will stop the trembling, and hasten the health from the cold illness. 
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear through fire baths or stinking pustules, which come from large corrupt substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	It is fitting in the first place, when they appear, that one makes a cautery on each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, the point of which is held in the fire, or of a long aristoloche root, or with a lentil-shaped cautery.  
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And always cauterize them at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they will not be able to grow further forward, but the superfluities from which they come are broken down, and they are healed. 
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Often there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the fire, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; 
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a very grievous thing to staunch. 
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press very hard until the blood is quieted under your finger, and that no drop issues anymore; 
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then put to the fire several small and large olive cauteries until they are all red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take one, large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the blood is stopped up. 
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it leaps when you lift your hand from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, immediately take another cautery which are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease to do one after another until the blood is drained. 
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And be careful that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient.  
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And know that when blood flows freely from the artery, one cannot properly rejoin it, especially if the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four methods which we have described. 
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not yet treated, or by strong ligature of thread, or by medicines placed upon it which have the power to rejoin blood.
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And let it be tied and strained carefully. 
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers a tightening of bandages or applies hot objects, or other similar things, it will not profit him nor the patient.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have a mirror or medicine present, they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it is rejoined above the wound and above the vein. 
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	And do not move the wound, but moisten it with cold water often as cold as possible until the blood is frozen and thickened and rests. 
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And make inquiries beforehand about those who need to be cauterized and medicated. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of cures by incision
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases where it is fitting to use fire cautery or burning medicines, and the incisions and the causes and instruments and forms of cauteries. 
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	And I have placed this chapter from the top down to the feet, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that those who want it can find it more easily. 
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter there often occurs evacuation of blood when opening a vein and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in extracting arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things.
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die. 
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	if some come who are so frightened by their illness that they die easily because of the fear they find in their illness and its severity. 
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and one must be afraid of these. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And there are some who give you their senses and say:  
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am cured." 
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the illness is insidious.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It does not suit you to consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not offer foolishly but wisely from those of whom you are certain, and whom you can take and lose. 
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	And use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients to which health is converted.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And this will help you to acquire great renown, glory, and lasting remembrance. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and rectitude, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordained this chapter in divisions by chapters, according to that which is before, or the chapter of cauteries, that I have devised from the head even to the feet so that you may more easily find that of which you will have need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	A head full of sharpness
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this ailment often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the child's head too forcefully. 
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	And sometimes it comes from an unknown cause. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this ailment except in children, and all those I have seen hastened death; 
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for this reason it seems to me better to leave these cures to others.  
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose shoulders were full of pain, and whose head grew larger each day until it could no longer support it; 
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture gathered under the bone above the diaphragm, between the heart and the bone;
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the works are such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you split near the head a wide crack; 
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and it should also be as long as two of us, as long as the moisture runs; 
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see this shape of the spatula:  
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs that you see are the corners of the head open on each side, and the sharp pain jumps forward when you press it with your hand inside, and this is not answered to you: 
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then it is fitting that you split near the head three fissures according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After removing the splits with cloths and powders, and he puts wine and oil, and leaves it like that until the fifth day; 
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then he unties it, and heals the wound with bandages and ointments, and leaves the head even, and gives the patient dry meat free of moisture to eat as long as the limb is strengthened and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess appears, and its gathering of sharpness; 
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for it is never in front; 
aucune fois derrier;	never behind; 
aucune fois en destre;	never to the right; 
et aucune fois en senestre.	and never to the left. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Therefore cut where the abscess appears, and the gathering of sharpness, and make the incision according to what power you have in it; 
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and be careful not to sever an artery;  
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and let the vein flow blood so that the patient dies from the depletion of blood and evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	From rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a sickness called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the breast, and the sickness is old, and medicine does not help, then the last resort is to cauterize with copper the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	Therefore, when you have cut them, it is fitting for the patient to put his head back;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	afterwards rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then remove the cloth from the patient's neck. 
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look where the vein beats, and the lobes of one and the other are behind the ears, and they are filled. 
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then mark the lobes with an incision, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts, until the vein reaches the bone, and this is done by the breadth of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatula under the artery and the cup above, cutting as much as it should through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if blood flows continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open to the touch, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space in three fingers, then mark and cut to the bone; 
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and the quantity of blood to be let out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can bear, and the fullness of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound: 
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If it remains on the bone with a slight pain, cut it so that pus does not come, then dress the wound and bandage it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	from a migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old headache comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and the heats in the temples and a head cold and similar things, and it is treated by methods of medicine cures and all that does not profit him at all, then we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the manner of extracting them is such that the patient should shave the hairs from his temples, and listen to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and is more full outside than in some men who are too cold; 
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	And if it is full, the patient should tighten his neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and raise the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly; 
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the spatulum of which this is the shape: 
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then draw it upwards with pincers, and detach it well from the membranes that are beneath it on each side; 
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is delicate, turn it to the point of the hook, then cut from that part according to the quantity of the two sides.  
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if she is not copied, then it will never jump all at once.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And treat the blood from the sixth hour until the third. 
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that decay does not come before the wound heals and blood flows. 
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then cut away the excess that is between the two ties in the same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize with a cutting cautery to the bone until the flesh is cut. 
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And this is the best work if the patient does not have a fever and they are of a hot complexion.  
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For cauteries help to finish the humors: 
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	for this reason it is of greater help against the humors.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	When it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one must fill the place with old cotton and put well-made tents on top. 
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are loosened, let it be treated with dry medicines that produce flesh, and with bandages, until it is healed; 
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if without cutting the artery as much as you work, so hurry to cauterize it, or apply vitriol and hold it in your hand so that the blood is stopped; 
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have this, place your finger on the area until the blood is congealed, and apply a sharp cold to the area so that the blood stops, and it is removed as it should be; 
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and that which is milder and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery of two parts, but the sharp points should be well spaced to keep their heat longer.  
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And there should be a space of one finger width between the two knives, and then when you have marked the two areas, and place the hot iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places. 
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and they shall be kept apart between the two heads for it is not soldered by this cautery at all. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the form of the cautery: 
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are running down the veins that are on the top of the head, and no remedy of medicine profits, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and his forehead shaking as if in a shiver; 
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and if they are swollen and moist so that the hairs of the papers are falling out, and the papers are being scorched and burned by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is needed.
