Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "the bruised remedy," and it is that you make at the back of the patient who has this illness three incisions on his forehead equally according to the length of the forehead. 
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the incisions be as it should go all along the forehead downwards to the nose, and the others let them be along the ribs above the papers, and beware of incising the arteries which are along the ribs above the papers 
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and remove your hand from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across joined 
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have ready a piece of sponge and much linen for wiping the blood, then put the spatula sharp on two parts as follows is its shape  
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is above the temple to the second incision;  
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape away all the flesh which is between the two incisions at all the tissue which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then extract with force this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first fissure, it is very sharp on one side and dull on the other; this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp edge towards the flesh burned at the heart, and the rounded edge towards the bone, and push until it comes to the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to those so that the incision is continuous until it reaches those which open onto the heart, and then likewise make in the middle a split until the other side. 
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	And then extract the blood equally, and press the place so that the blood is taken up. 
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then put in each split a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths softened in wine and oil and ash, and keep that no abscesses come there. 
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And on the third day untie the bandage, and he will administer a large poultice of hot water, then cure it with ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other cures as one cures wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	where the eyes are
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When someone has an acute catarrh accustomed to it, and you see the eyes are swollen and small, and weaken the vision, and the papers are burned.  
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	And the hair falls out, or the head aches with sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; 
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Then know by these signs that these humors and phlegm do not come from only one vein, and the best cure for it is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you must instruct the patient to place his hand behind his forehead, then make a large incision between the forehead and a broad space on the cheek.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin at the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the cut be down to the bone; 
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples which move when one chews;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then put cotton wool between the two edges of the incision, and bind it with linen cloth; 
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind cloths soaked in wine and oil over it, and beware of a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, you must rub the bone until fresh flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents which promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere:	In such a manner: 
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster. 
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	And administer it to these wounds in order to draw out flesh throughout. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	Either grain, or beast, or stone from a mine, or similar thing such as iron. 
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	Or seed, such as acorns, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Or flowing things such as water and saliva and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When there is a stone or another manner of thing in the ear that does not fit in the ear nor grow in it, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, if it distills any drop of oil of violets or oil of sesame seed, then administer extraction. 
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	And make it sneeze by compressing, and plug the nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool. 
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and hold the ear above. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times comes fever from this treatment; 
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come fever, administer extraction with fine tweezers, of which here is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps fever with tweezers, it is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, administer extraction with a fine lancet of small sharpness; 
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not jump by this, make a cane of iron and insert the head of the cane or the hole of the ear strongly, and stuff what is around the cane with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane; 
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then the fever will form, for many times fever comes as we have said; 
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come fever in any way, take glutin with which birds are caught, and put into some instrument suitable for this, and put a piece of cotton around;  
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the buttocks onto the stone or whatever it may be, and draw hard. 
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come out with all the things we have said, then hasten to slit the ear just as you would an abscess that is hot or a spasm. 
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the manner of the slitting is that you first make the patient dizzy from the cephalic vein, and draw out some blood according to his constitution. Then have the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small slit at the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; 
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the slit be crescent-shaped, so that you reach the bone, then suck out the pus according to your ability, and quickly suck it into your mouth; 
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And continue the treatment until it is healed.  
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grain that is within and it swells, then administer extraction; 
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin, delicate spatula according to this form:  
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; 
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with delicate pincers and a syringe, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	When a patient has sharp pain in the ear, it is necessary for them to first use sneezing as a remedy and generously fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on the same ear where the pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps forcefully through this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, then take many stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and heat them a little over the fire; 
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and place the patient's ear in a hole or opening, and press on it with his feet from the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; 
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop doing this stone by stone until all the pain is gone, and so it will all be gone; 
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see it, take the joint, and put one of the heads into the ear, and take the other head and heat it with fire until the softer joint is burned; 
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then redo another part of other joints until all the pain is gone, as we have said in the stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	For the extraction of a small animal, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; 
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large enough to be felt, use pincers for its extraction;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	For the extraction of worms embedded in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and where we discuss distillations, and the treatment does not help at all, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sunlight: 
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are any worms, take them out with delicate pincers; and if there are none, take the cane whose form is this: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	Insert the most delicate tip into the ear according to the amount of the patient's suffering, then suck up the whole cane; 
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey and come out, stuff cotton around the cane as I have said for the stone; 
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them or a treatise on distillations; 
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, whose form is this as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether of silver or iron three holes are below at the small openings, and above covers for distilling. 
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	And to press the distillation inside, there is an iron instrument well made for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap cotton around the point.  
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	Then put your oil or juice in it, and whatever medicine you see fit in the cane, and hold the cane to the ear. 
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then put the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or reaches the ear. 
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And let the patient smell it inside, and whether the distillation is a bit heated by the fire or not, you distill it into the ear.  
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be careful that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be as good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have some perforation in their ears; 
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	And the same thing happens to adults by rupture of a wound, or from a splinter lodged in the ear, and this rupture sometimes comes perfectly within the ear, if one cannot see it; 
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And sometimes a small piece of fire obstructs the perforation, and one sees it well.  
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes perfectly within and cannot be seen is a grievous ailment in many conditions, and in this case it is fitting that you place the patient's ear in the sun; 
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:  
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	If you see the apparent obstruction, if the work has all this sputum, this is its form: 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	It should be sharp and cutting in front and behind, so that it does not injure the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the hair is from the flesh or earlobe, hold it with delicate pincers and clip lightly until all of the hair is removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is performed perfectly in the ear, then take a delicate razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then apply it to the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the hair which causes pain to the patient's ear, pierce lightly and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear. 
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.  
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and powder it with ground vitriol. 
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear is swollen, it is necessary that you remove the tent and insert another moistened with cerate made of rose oil and wax until the swelling is removed. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, plunge a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding, which are or treatments of distillations.
de la char des papieres	From the flesh of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This instrument which comes on papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is fitting that you extend them with pincers and forceps, and the cup of a spatula from its roots; 
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then put on the place powdered vitriol. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without cutting off, then cauterize with a lentil-shaped cautery subtly, and after the incision cauterize it worthily. 
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	And often repair them, so that nothing remains of their roots; 
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not return.  
de la gresle	From gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come on papers of the eyes things that seem like hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called “hail,” and it is an assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; 
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such: 
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take care if the hail moves from one side to the other, and this is a light thing to know; 
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Make then the two sides wide, then lightly scrape each part, then take it with pincers and cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of paper, do not grieve anything to the patient;  
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the fissure is large, sew it with a suture and treat it until it is healed. 
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not exert any force, for ointments will soon restore it and bring flesh.  
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the hail is descending into the inside of the ear toward the upper part, invert the paper and extend the hail with pincers, cut it and press from one side and the other; 
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not matter. 
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the hailstone is cut out, apply oil of salt water and heal the place with that which draws heat until the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease which is drawn into cloths of paper and it happens more to children than to adults, and it grieves much their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes. 
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and for this they lie on their faces then, and sleep on them, and have their papers beneath their eyebrows wet so that the swelling and appearance are covered with exinach which appears in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your thumbs and feel the exirnach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in a healthy place;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	And then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that it contains to be drawn from each part, then put it on top. 
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	And press with your hands on one side and the other so that the discharge is gathered within the circle. 
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	Then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit about as wide and no larger than the wound made when opening a vein. 
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	And make the skin whole until you reach the discharge. 
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in several arrangements, the discharge comes from the slit according to the shape of a piece of white fat.  
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Therefore extract it all at once with a piece of cloth pinched between your hands, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is scattered.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	And be careful that you do not add anything into the fissure, unless you reach the whole septum as far as the eye, lest you bruise it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the pus does not appear at the beginning of the fissure, then slightly widen the fissure until it appears. 
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the spot, and bind with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind flaxseed and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, then let the cure of softening poultices be applied until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow from grafted skin that are not natural and are old, they harm the eyes, and bring about various illnesses such as accustomed tears and softening of the skin and albuginea, as long as it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And the treatment is according to four methods: 
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before it, or a chapter of cautery, and is done either by incision and suture, or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient on your breast, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand; 
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is converted, it is good; 
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, if you put a needle through all of it above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let this be at the edge of the paper where the hairs grow at these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; 
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, across the whole span, from the large tear duct to the small; 
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then draw on the paper a shape like an myrtle leaf, and in any case it is necessary that the shape be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided into all.  
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if one needs to apply a large quantity of paper, according to how soft the paper is; 
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make across all the spatula on the two lines that you have marked, and begin with large tears to small; 
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs, as thick as a radish root, then push the scalpel into one of the two angles of the heart, then flay it all; 
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then bring together the two lips with a stitch from a needle using very fine thread, wipe away the blood, and let the excess of threads dry on the two eyebrows with nothing sticky, if you see fit to do so; 
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and threads until three or four days; 
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then heal the wound without stitching with drying and constricting things, for paper will revive at the closure of the wound and its joining, but stitching is harmful (as the ancients say), and this work is without fear. 
et si a une autre maniere:	And if there is another way: 
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And it is that you sign the paper in a shape like the leaf of myrtle as we have told, at III ounces dried according to the form that is here:  
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then he who has small strength should apply it equally according to the form which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the tweezers and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread and put it in the shape; 
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put one other thread under the large tear, and the second thread under the small one, and bring together between your fingers the threads equally; 
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand equally and lift all the skin on which you have signed as we have told, then bring together the two edges of the wound by stitching and heal it until it is healed;  
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments. 
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	And it sometimes happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: 
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	If you must use what we have said about incision; 
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	But the suture in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of boils is according to this form:  
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	And convert the paper and place it within according to what I have said, then make two boils by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and as wide as a spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	And take two ends of two parts where you hold the threads; 
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then join one and the other subtly above what rises from the oil of the paper, and draw the two boils from the two parts formed;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	And leave it like this for several days
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If he delays, so that the wound has some strength, then heal it until it is healthy; 
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound heals and if the paper is lifted and they no longer prick the hairs; 
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure and according to this quantity of length and width:  
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The work is such that you take a fine needle and put in a very fine silk thread; 
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then join the ends and knot them subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; 
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then order in the chase another fine silk thread tightly and knot the two ends of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's head on a healthy surface; 
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	And let it be under the sun so that the work is illuminated, because it is a subtle and delicate work, then put the needle all the way into the root of the hair hastily, and make it pierce through the paper quickly as you draw it over the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull out the hair up to the flesh, and put that hair into the flesh, if there is one or two or three or more. 
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then pull out your hand so that the hairs come out at all the flesh in the paper with the natural hair.  
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the flesh is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will treat the flesh below all the thread that you have ordered there, until the flesh comes out through the holes above it, and you see it by the sight of the eye. 
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you will treat the flesh and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh grows up.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, then accompany one long horsehair with the natural ones, and let it grow together with the one you leave it with until it is lengthened and then remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the putrefaction of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this illness which is called "aleacratio" or gangrene comes to the eye, it can happen in two ways: 
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by cutting of a wound, or a cut or a cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way to treat it is that you split that suture and separate the lips of it and put linen tents inside and bind it until it is healed; 
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not right that you use things in its treatment that dry and constrict.  
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first; 
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; 
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and rose water or elderflower and flax seed are cooked, and ointments of diascordium melted in any oil, and he envelops a tent and cures it this way.  
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal according to the shape it was before. 
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And this work that we have said is nothing other than directions for this illness, so that it does not return to the shape it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This sickness which is below, which is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	Accidents come from wounds and fissures and cautery and similar things; 
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of the work is this: you take a needle with a doubled thread and insert it into the flesh, making it pierce from the left tear duct to the right so that the thread comes out in two sides of the flesh; 
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then you spread the flesh above the needle and sew it with a spatula half a span wide.  
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is fitting, it is good; 
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, take a razor and put it in the slit, and turn the paper, and make two slits on either side of the inside of the paper. 
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	Let the heads of the two slits be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make one angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a letter that has no "Greek I"; 
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that flesh, according to the amount its sides are thick underneath, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts and sew them with a thread of wool; 
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the care that we have said of softening remedies, and bandages, until it is healed.  
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a slit or seam or cautery, it is fitting that you make a full slit below the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said before; 
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then sever between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; 
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare themselves with all their power to make the figure return to its natural form; 
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patients themselves, according to what work and instruments are needed, must be in several positions.  
dou soudement de la papiere	with the help of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this suture occurs in the hands of men in such a way that the paper above is glued with the white of an egg, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must put the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; 
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and hold it with forceps, as long as you cut what is exposed with a very fine spatula, which is not too sharp or too dull, so that the patient does not suffer because the spatula is too sharp and does not burn the oil; 
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	And let your incision, which you scrape away from the assembly, be light so that the paper comes back according to its natural form. 
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	And it heals all the assembly, and make no more in the sharp eye salty, and lift it from sharp sweetness, and of colic. 
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then put between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and put wool soaked in plenty of egg on the oil. 
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after the third day, use warm colic and things southward until it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners: 
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and seeming like hard fat, and another which is not nervous, but is seeming like white frozen moisture, that when you touch it with iron and think to pinch it, it cannot. 
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and one and the other such beginning towards the large tear duct, and grows bit by bit until it covers the whole eye and all the light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is such that the patient puts his head on a sound surface, then opens his eyes; 
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper with your hand, then place the needle at the tips of the small forceps, and extend it above; 
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put in horsehair or cowhair or oxhair, and strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a bit and put it in the needle, and pierce it all the way through with the needle, and tie the needle to a thread and extend it above, and flay all the hair on the side of the needle which touches the eyelid and the silk to the hair up to the head, then cut off the rest at the root of the tear duct all along the delicate spatula and with small forces, and leave the flesh natural or tear duct, so that by the incision the body's accustomed tears do not come;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and at no time have the nails been put to the oncicle alone, as we said. 
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then we flay the whole spatula bone so that it is shaped like this: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the little plum is not pierced; 
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, put a piece of silk thread into the eye, and a collar made of silver, and leave it until the next day; 
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it as needed until it is healed.  
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot put in the needle, and the oncicle cannot enter, this type of nail is often cured with medicine; 
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and it grows as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, open the eye of the patient, and take the spatula with a small sharp point according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And place the ungent on top subtly, and if you see that it diminishes nothing and the reason hastens it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red lead, and only grind it, and stop the eye until the next day; 
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing stands in your way, such as a boil in the eye, then milk it and first treat the hot boil until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear ducts harms the eye greatly, then suspend it to a thread, and in a cup cover part and not all, so that a stream of tears does not come; 
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In some men, flesh-colored warts never arise, and cover the plum kernel and bind it on papers and turn it over the fire, and it resembles a rose of baluster; 
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And the work is such that the patient puts his head in your lap, then you perform the operation on him, and keep all those parts clean with suitable bandages, and support it with strength. 
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then shave the first part, and go shaving all the way to the end with a razor, and be careful not to injure the eye during the operation. 
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And make the incision with a spatula as we have said in the incision of the nail, and use small force so that you remove the splinter, as the form after this chapter demonstrates.  
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	And when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of cypress that has been boiled or distilled with red copper and similar corrosive medicines, and put hot cotton soaked in oil on top, so it is secure from a hot abscess.  
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it remains there and the foot swells up, and you doubt a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess; 
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Then return to your work while it is healing, and do the same as many times as the object is inserted into the eye in this manner. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nevertheless, it is fitting that you relieve the treatment of each weak eye from its natural path;  
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental path in ironwork; 
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	And do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member suffers from the work.  
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Beneath are red veins which are covered upon the eye, and they tolerate at sight their work and weaken the eye all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	Therefore, it is necessary first to look at whether the eye is strong or weak and there is no other illness except pain; 
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then proceed in this way:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in good health, then suspend those veins at all ounce according to his wisdom, and let the ounces be subtle double according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be placed in two rows upon the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then one coils as strongly those veins subtly, and wipes the blood hour after hour, until you see remove those veins outside of the eye; 
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and guard that you do not prick the eye at the points of the spatulas, and make this work at noon hour in front of the sun, and be very ardent in your work so that you only cut those veins; 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, if you distill in the eye colire green and red to corrupt that which has remained within the eye. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you do not have power to pluck all that in that hour, if you make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of it, and leave some days until the pain is soothed and you are sure of hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; 
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the shape of the strengths: 
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The one named "fistula" is made.
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it by cautery and burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then cut into the abscess where it should remain and drain all the moisture until the bone is exposed.  
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed and you see decay and blackness, then cut it with all the instruments in this shape. 
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And it is called "sharp chief" and is made of strong iron at the head front, and is pointed like a file as it is in this present shape. 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers and press with your hand a bit until you know that corruption is gone.  
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wound is soldered and flesh grows, and the body of the bowel is soldered and remains so for forty days, and it does not reopen nor become abscessed, and no ill accidents occur, know that it is healed. 
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If this is not the case, if there is nothing else to do but bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: 
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	And that you uncover the bone the second time with an iron instrument and sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take a borer according to this form, and let the head of the borer have three angles, and the drill bit be sharpened down to the point as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then put it on the bone near the tear duct, and keep your hand away from the eye by one finger's breadth, then turn the borer completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the vein in this place will swell if they hold their hand over their nose.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the place, it goes to the snow; 
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	From the outflow of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eye opens completely and there is no disturbance in the nose, or diminishment, then you must bind the patient; 
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the sound, then apply cupping glasses or a hot iron to draw out pus, then put on the eye a bandage made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye, and plaster it with bandages and cloths;  
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough and fold each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then strain it with a hard bandage, and start the cupping glasses to suck without cutting. 
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the cupping glasses and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the ligaments soften, then you must strain it more. 
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the oil come back together, it is good. 
se ce non;	If not;  
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	Start the plaster and bandages and bandage and cupping glasses again until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	For the tearing of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When ruptures come in the canvas weave, then open it and take out thin sheets like grains of resin, and they are wonderful to see.  
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see it covered, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then thrust another needle where it has a doubled thread from the tear.  
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and have it pierced, and leave the first needle according to its position; 
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then grasp the place of the double thread and tie one part of the eye around it, and pull it tight, then remove the needle and put a softened linen cloth soaked in plenty of egg white; 
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the threads adhere with the eye, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; 
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and once the wound is held by the eye on each side with a circle of cloth, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye shows great swelling, pierce it with a delicate scalpel that comes out perfectly from the eye, and drain the albuminous moisture and reduce the swelling, and it will subside soon; 
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed. 
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bowel of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than bowel which is gathered in the eye, resembling descending aqueduct, and it is not aqueduct; 
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands in two parts, and move it until you see the bowel coming up to your eyes. 
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be fixed, and not descend, and let the light be unhindered, and have the patient look at things as he used to; 
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is aqueduct, and if the descent of the bowel is not as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a subtle spatula and place it on the cornea with a prick by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as long as the bowel rises; 
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is removed, if you distill in sharp hot oil mixed with honey, or sharp or fenugreek boiled and honey, then let it be cured by another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	sharp points of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen similar things in the division, and what it takes to pierce; 
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if in work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is fitting that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, far from the light of the sun, and bind the good eye tightly; 
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper from the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; 
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right; 
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument behind the cornea at the thickness of a reed in the white part of the eye towards the part with the lesser tear duct. Then push the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and twist your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; 
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And it is necessary that the measure of the almagda path be equal to the measure of the space from the pupil to the end of the black part; 
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the cornea of the eye; 
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone through this paper because of the clarity of the corneal membrane, then place the instrument up to where the point is, and then press it down one path after another.  
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the sharp point descends now, let the patient see it in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	Afterwards rest a little, and if the point goes back up the second path, put force with the instrument, and when it is well embedded and it does not rise, then gently extract the almagda by turning your hand little by little; 
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	And then put again a sharp point of a gem stone, and lift from it the oil inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a compress of oiled wool or linen soaked in rose oil and egg yolk, and bandage with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on common broth with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then you must take the instrument that is called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And pierce then only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deeply, but make a subtle place, then put in almond paste, as we have said; 
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and for the completion of the work prepare the patient a doctor approaching, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; 
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and let it be free from all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let it be bound according to its position until the third day; 
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then unbind him in the same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day; 
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not fitting that you do this during the time of healing or after the incision now, but it is fitting that you delay it because the sharpness rises quickly.  
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	When an abscess comes, untie the oil before the seventh day, and direct it by he who soothes abscesses. 
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is appeased, untie the view and put on its face a little gold to cover for any day, and let it be in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then leave from the house bit by bit, and turn into your cases.
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And know that no disciples should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country people made almond milk, which one sucks for sharpness, but nevertheless I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read about it in books of the ancients. 
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the resemblances of almond forms, for those who do not know them to see. 
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be of proper iron 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the last one in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh out of the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there are born or made various jointed charms, of which some appear to be scorpions with many feet. 
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	And if there are such that it has a charm enchanted of fox color, and if a charm of good bone color.  
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that case of these charms which is of good bone and not enchanted, it befits that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun. 
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	And open his nostrils, and give the charm to those nostrils, and draw forth 
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	for as long as you know that the charm is entirely drawn out.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains anything that you cannot draw out, then work at it with all the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains. 
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if without you surpassing it, or abscess grows, then cut it as it suits; 
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize them until the pus is dried up and all the humors are removed, then pour or mix easily and sharply with wine. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the mixture works, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed; 
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is a humor embedded in the bone above, to which the instruments cannot come to cut; 
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then it is necessary that you put in a thread of linen a bit thick, and knotted by hand with us, and have between each knot a space of one inch or less; 
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's shoulder with the thread in his nose so that it can pull it through the nose into the mouth; 
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	And many times do children thus make fools of themselves, and it is a light thing for him who wishes to do it. 
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other as those who are at the loom.  
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the new ones have corrupted this flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back at the beginning as before. 
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corrupted all that remains of the flesh. 
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	And then place at the beginning a cane of lead for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, then use them. 
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, into which one distills oils and medicines or such. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it is made of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and the same applies to its conduit. 
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, make it a closed cane, and let the instrument be full for purging the head;  
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and it has a handle at the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh out of the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Often a disease called "telul" arises on the head and grows large, so much so that it is a frightening thing to behold. 
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And for this reason, you must cut it off at the beginning and remove all of it, then apply a cautery or burning medicine to the spot. 
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if it is delayed in being cut until it is large, then be careful if it is hard, of dark color, and lacking sensation. 
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not touch it with iron, for it is an infected abscess, for when it is cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; 
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can be completely cut, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with drying and binding agents.
