quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilage works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, to see if the wound is fresh and bleeding freely;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bring the two edges together in stitches, and then treat it until it is healed; 
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they bleed, then bring the two edges together in stitches, and hold them firm, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and ground incense over them; 
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put on the powders a piece of plaster of Paris or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it dries out by itself, then cure it with anointing until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The way to suture is that you bring together the solution: 
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	either with needles, as we have said in suturing the belly; 
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have shown you.  
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Sometimes hands appear within the lips of a hard abscess, resembling grains of millet, both smaller and larger; 
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn back the lips and split open each knot, and take them with forceps and cut them in every part; 
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the place after incision with powdered vitriol until the blood is cleansed;  
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then wash it with oil, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed. 
de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there grows on the gums hot flesh, which the ancients called "albulus"; 
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run; 
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put ground vitriol on the spot, or other binding and drying powders; 
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it; 
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes there are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; 
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth are black and citron-colored and wormy, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling; 
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	If it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulders be in your lap, and cut the flesh or the bones that appear, until nothing remains. 
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And then make black and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are clean. 
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if one removes what is at the first reason, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have cut everything. 
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that teeth need various forms of instruments for cutting, according to what the work demonstrates, for the rasp which cuts out teeth has other shapes than those which cut between the teeth.  
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these shapes and others should be prepared with you. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay the extraction as much as you can, for it should not be done hastily. 
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for the razor 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to be treated, it is fitting that you are certain of the teeth which are doing the treating.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks that it is from a toothache, and makes the good tooth bleed; 
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and nevertheless the pain does not go away because of this, as long as the bad tooth remains, for we have often wanted to do this to those healers; 
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is fitting that you scrape around the tooth at all its sides, strongly in order to keep the gum from all sides; 
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it with your two hands or use delicate pliers at the first touch and touch, until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the pliers;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the jaw of the patient be in your holy hand between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert the end into each side lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the bone is pierced and gnawed, it is fitting that you fill it with cloths where the holes are. 
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	And if you extract it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break when extracted. 
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And it is very wise to work around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and a part remains, and returns to the patient by the evil of the root, greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not do as the ignorant barber-surgeons do, who by their haste and boldness break the jawbone sometimes, and do not bring about what we have related.  
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	But they sometimes bring about great illness by the extraction because of the roots that remain or the jawbone that they break, as we have often seen. 
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or ale and salt.  
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if a flow of blood comes, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the place. 
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And if that does not work, then cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments with which one must first pull out teeth should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you are pulling the tooth.  
et ce sont les formes:	And these are the shapes: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they shall be of large members so that they do not bend at all against, and shall be made of well-forged iron, and shall have teeth to hold the pieces.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you put moistened cotton soaked in butter on the place for one or two days until the gums are softened, then insert the tongs called "algefri," whose head resembles a bird's beak. 
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	And they should be made inside like a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And it must be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out with this, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, help yourself with all the instruments, from which the following forms come: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two handles, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments which are placed in front of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be such that they cannot break, and know that many instruments are dense;  
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted; 
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and clever master surgeons find their own instrument according to what their work and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of others, so that it does not break the chariot or other bones, or rot if he seeks the instruments that suit it, as I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, from which is its form:  
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-gripping to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; 
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with suitable medicines, and if it has decay in the bone, and it is small, so do all this with instruments. 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When a tooth does not appear according to nature and the form is ugly, even in young women, you should know if the density is born after the tooth and is not in its proper place, and it cannot be filed or smoothed. 
adonques lou raie;	Then the ray. 
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument which has this shape and resembles a small beak, and is made of sharp iron. 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the chisel little by little in your hand for several days for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then the file with a part files as follows is its form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	And it is like the file with which one makes needles.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	And file the tooth little by little in your hands lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks off.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Then the plane at the end should have no razor sharpness, and if it is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file down the sharpness until it is even so that it does not cut the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	When a tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When a tooth in front falls out, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot bite on what he eats without pain, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and that does not work; 
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes. 
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see that you need to straighten the teeth, take the thread and wrap it twice between the two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the crooked teeth, if there is one or several, until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side; 
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then begin again the covering up to the part where you began, and hold your hand delicately and wisely, so that it does not move. 
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let your bandage be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then grasp the head with forceps and bring them together, and place it between the sound tooth, and set it so that it does not bruise the tongue.  
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then leave it thus tightly as long as it can remain, and if it loosens or the threads break, bind it with another thread. 
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains and serves thus for its entire duration, this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two sound teeth and the two missing ones, as you see.  
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the head of the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, again and again, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let no one interfere who is not wise and experienced, and at no time is the shape of a cow's bone tooth made, and it is put in the place where the defect is, and it is extracted as we have said, and remains and serves thus for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the bond of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	At no time does this ligament which comes below the tongue or by nature, come to be so.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	Or by accident of a stitched wound; 
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	And the work is such that you open the patient's mouth, and hold his head in your lap, and lift the tongue; 
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then grasp the nervous ligament broadly, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knotting, and it is due to stitching of a wound, then he puts in the hook and grasps broadly that ligament;  
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and guard that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is beneath; 
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done so, lift the place with sharp rose and water, or with sharp cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; 
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and let the patient chew each night so that the gums cannot adhere.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if blood flow comes, put powdered vitriol on the place; 
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if it continues to bleed, cauterize it with a lentil cautery, which is good for this.  
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then cure it with other cures until it is healed, 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it of a dark color or black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; 
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is leaning toward the blind spot, and there is moisture, if it drips, one cuts the corner of a delicate spatula and frees it on one side and the other. 
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	And if your effort does not succeed in your work, put crushed vitriol on it until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you draw out all the pus. 
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then lift the place with ease and silk, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes boils come inside the throat which are called "godaths," and they are properly called the two almonds; and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: 
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is a hard abscess of small sense and dark color, do not touch it with iron at all.  
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron at all, so as not to cause bloodletting. 
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But leave it alone until it is dead, and then you will cut it off, or it will break on its own. 
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is white and the root is thin, have your instrument ready to cut, but first see if the abscess is warm, relaxed and soothed. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and let their head be in your hand, and open their mouth and take the instrument between your hands, and press down on the tongue with it.  
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And let it be of silver or thin steel like a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	As you press the tongue down with this instrument and see the abscess, take a lancet and put it into the almond (tonsil) and pull hard on it as much as you can. 
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and do not handle anything from the cloths with it, then apply the cautery instrument, of which this is the form, that it seems one force; 
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all its edges are curved, and one edge against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel. 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, take pliers as they are of this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And it should be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other.  
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have applied one of the almonds, then apply the other according to the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot, sharp water and easy, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with hot water, or decoctions of cooked pomegranate seeds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stemmed. 
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then let it heal until it is sound.  
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And sometimes other abscesses are born in the throat than the two almonds, so treat them like the two almonds. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, namely an abscess of small size. 
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And it had almost completely closed off the whole throat so that the woman could not breathe through the passage which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained in that state for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high up that he had to put two reins through the two holes of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened immediately, and put a poultice in it, then I drew out the pus freely and drew out a large portion of pus. 
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then I did another poultice in the other opening where it was born, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue.  
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	Afterwards I put poultices on these abscesses, and squeezed out some of it, and only a little blood came out. 
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus was the conduit of her throat unstopped, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut from that abscess for a long time; 
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess would grow again, and fill the place which I had emptied, until it became very large; 
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I lanced it and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	thus it ceased to grow; 
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I departed from these parts, and only God knows what happened to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the cold descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; 
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is below large and round, it is called "eye". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the sore abscess is quieted, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; 
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one which is round assembled and is not long; 
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is of blood color or brown color or black, then you must avoid its incision. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the sick person.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, by its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before; 
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the lancet into the eye, and draw it downwards, and hold it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned for the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut away more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural boundary; 
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut away more, it will greatly grieve the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and dress it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of the cautery, it is fitting that you apply something to numb the fear during cauterization.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and pointed.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And let the patient put his head in clean water, and then press his tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and seize it with sharp, lively tongs, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; 
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And apply the point of this instrument, which has this form:  
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And it has on its head a hair or where one puts the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument on all the medicine above the eye; 
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And let the patient lie on his side so that his saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend into the throat, and cause harm. 
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, for a quantity of half an hour, until you see it soften and the stinging of the medicine is appeased; 
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in medicine, and push the instrument all the way into the cotton along its length until the cotton ignites on the edge. 
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry and apply it after four or five days.  
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to renew the cautery with medicine, do so again and after the cautery wipe it around the edge with cotton dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine. 
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be treated with cold water, and be healed with gargles until it is cured.  
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery. 
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is cured with fumigation according to this method, take calament and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and add water, and boil.  
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and let the pot have the instrument stuck in it according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be of silver or steel, and let one of the heads be put in the mouth of the sick person so that the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, as long as the eye is mortified; 
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	then repeat often, until the eye dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the arrival of a hot abscess, for many things happen; 
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do this except when the hot abscess is declining. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put in the head a bit of egg white, so that the mouth of the sick person is not too hot; 
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the egg white does not make the vapor burden the mouth, and it is a good cure together with safety.  
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times a bone or fishbone, or something else, gets stuck in the throat. 
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So it is necessary that you draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with the whole instrument, so that you see the thing move. 
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what you do not see and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach. 
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	Perhaps the thing will come out by vomiting.
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	Or if the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of stale bread. 
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	And tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	And when it arrives at its place, it will come loose, and then you will draw it out forcefully. 
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come easily from what we have said, then take an instrument of lead according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised upward; 
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it cause his death, nor push any bone inside; 
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument in, so that he knows where the thing is located; 
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if it goes down, or if he pulls it out forcefully and evenly with all the instrument until it comes loose. 
de la sansue de la gorge	from the vein of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes medicine alone is enough for a remedy, as I have said in the division on the treatment of remedies; 
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, and press their tongue with the instrument that I have described for you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, if it is grasped by all its small hooks, or with delicate tongs that are suited for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a dog's cane and put it in the patient's throat, then push or shove the end of the cane with a hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And keep the patient warm every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a full vial of cold water, and work the mouth open, and put it in your mouth all at once, and move it around in your hand often; 
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And as soon as the bone feels the cold, it will fall back into place. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not fall back into place as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; 
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall back into place without delay. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and it be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and the head of the instrument be put through that hole;  
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you put in your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes up to the bone.  
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And the wound will now heal, and if it does not close, begin fumigation many times. 
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And the patient suffers thirst, and eats salty things and such, and does not drink water. 
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And then it will be necessary that she be healed by this treatment. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it can be seen, resembles curved tongs to enter the throat. 
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it has the appearance of a beak of a sewing needle, and it has the roughness of a file, so that what it takes, it cannot let go. 
et vez ci la forme:	And see this shape:  
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many types of abscesses are, according to what memory comes here after one and another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size.  
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways one of which is in its own likeness, and of that which it holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the boils when they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the buttocks, and abscesses in fleshy areas are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if to abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the belly is healed according to its fulfillment;  
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if to such as it befits to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, like abscesses which are near joints.  
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and they are left until they are ripe around it, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is healed, it will harm the principal limb;  
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or where it is near the foundation, if one pierces it even when it is healed; 
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it does not behoove that you pierce an abscess ripe without complete digestion, except that which is near the foundation, lest it rot through and through, and be lengthened within, and a fistula arises;   
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal greatly. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know the time for the perforation of the abscess which is dangerous according to its completion, and that is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and from the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; 
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you must make the perforation where the most dependent part of the abscess is, and where it appears to move;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the perforation should be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or at joints and nerves and arteries, it should be made in all their equals where there is no danger of a tear. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to the position of that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in fleshy tissue, it is best that you leave the opening until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this time, the poison will spread along the body, and it will be filled with a lot of filth; 
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps the lips and the depth of it harden. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that needs to be pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the limbs require.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is fitting that you administer small abscesses, small perforations; 
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many fissures according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is fitting to cut out the core, and cover; 
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become as yellow as drapery, and is mortified, then it is fitting to do as one does with boils: 
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such of which one cuts as the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of angers; 
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuttings. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, it is fitting that you pierce it completely; 
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and when the abscess is large and it has gathered much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but draw out a part; 
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then repack the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing further. 
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this many times one after the other, until all the pus has come out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Likewise if the patient is weak in constitution, or a woman bearing child, or small children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the entrails often leap with the expulsion of the bowels, so that by chance the patient dies, and you are not to blame.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if you wipe the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; 
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a clean cut, apply bandages of linen or fine cotton. 
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess with many openings, it is necessary that you place a bandage in each one so that they come together. 
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have covered a part of the skin in the abscess and have sewn it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day. 
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the bone should be set and treated with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water that is sharp and clear, moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding site many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the discharge of blood persists, apply dressing and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is the time of winter, and the wound or abscess is very sensitive, then you must place bandages and cloths softened in wine and hot oil. 
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the flesh is strong, then you should put damp cloths soaked in vinegar and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; 
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open the abscess, wipe it clean, and treat it as is necessary until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is something that must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: 
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter. 
des soros	of the shoulders
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When boils come on the head, they are like little knots that are in rags, just as the seam of a chemise, and many look alike.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and others that have moisture as well as pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are those that are hard and stony at the edges, there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is such that you must test all instruments which are called “entromissoire”, from which the form comes after this, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, let him pass a long cloth over it.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, do not leave any skin containing that moisture exposed, for it will return if you leave anything.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; 
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; 
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and do this for what remains overnight. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds a thick pus, then cut it according to this form for a long time;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and drain your lancets, and flay it from all sides, and apply all your treatment to draw out the pus where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery opposes you, do as I told you afterward. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for an abscess if it is pierced, and from the waist and from the healer as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the abscess pierces and moistens, it is lighter, because they are drops of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses or boils have no moisture, and of those was one I lanced on the head of an old woman; 
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess just like a hard stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; 
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had struck it, they would have done as much harm as striking a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	For other boils that come on the head, such as those which come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be made in the lowest place, so that the pus can flow out; 
et les cure si com il covient.	and the treatment should be done accordingly.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess occurs in the neck and below the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes it comes in other parts of the body, and they are many and interconnected with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And every scrofula is properly within its own rib, just as the wart and the boil on the head, as we have said; 
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the resemblances of these scrofula are many 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some which contain moisture, and if there are malignant ones which do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one then which you see of good disposition to touch, and resembles the color of the body, and moves from every part and is not near the nerves of the neck or the artery or the vein, and is not deep; 
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	it is fitting that you cut it above, and flay it from every part, and extend the two edges of the sore to one-quarter inch, if you need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; 
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel neither be blunt nor too sharp, so that the hands do not slip, and do not see too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that stop blood, and remove the wound;  
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And leave it until the abscess is calmed and the wound softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood has been drained off, return to your work until you have completed it. 
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then let your thumb indicate if there are any small scrofulas, and cut and clean them.  
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not right to cut that scrofula at its root. Rather tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall away by itself without harm. 
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out all the scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them up now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary for you to understand how to cut the root of it, and draw force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, pierce them where they appear dead;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it as the one mentioned before, depending on it, then administer tents with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption. 
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleansed, apply an ointment promoting flesh, until it heals. 
de squinance	from squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; 
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have a squint, it is fitting that the fissure in the throat called the "epiglottis" be scraped;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and this should not be done for them, because all the veins and the pores of the patient are closed to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the almonds. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the throat, it is necessary to lift the epiglottis to prevent death from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore fitting, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four, a small incision across, between the two circles or according to the amount of the incision in the soft palate, not in the cartilage;  
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those are suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis because there is no cartilage and the vessels are long to inquire. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is fitting that he extends the skin of the throat to all its extent, then splits the flesh as far as it reaches the channel. 
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the syfac as we have said; 
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel that flows out through the place that is broken, and by the absence of the voice. 
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open a while.  
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed in which we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the flesh and sew it all alone without the cartilage. 
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines which cause flesh to grow, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely torn open, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault lies with the windpipe.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death. 
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And because the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. Then they commanded to sew the wound and clean it, until it was clean. 
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I have seen. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took a knife and stabbed it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the lung. 
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to heal her, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood which had issued from it, and although it had not yet pierced a vein nor gone further than the throat, the veins were weak through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed the wound, and I cleaned it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And it happened to the maiden that she became hoarse of voice, and afterwards returned to her usual state. 
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called “hernia of the throat,” and is a large abscess in the color of jaundice, and occurs mostly in women. 
et est selonc II manieres:	And it occurs in two ways:  
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Where the natural has no cause. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two ways, of which one is similar to fat boils, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us of the artery. 
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there should be fear, and it is not fitting to work with fire except on that which is small, and test and examine at every opening: 
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as soft as our butter and cannot flow through any vein, cut off the top as we cut noses and treat all its hairs if there are any. 
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and bandage it well from the start, and heal it as is appropriate until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways are known to us of which I will say all the resemblances; 
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is fitting that I state all the differences that exist between a vein and an artery.  
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that an artery is hot and feverish as long as the boiling is not past and the decay is completed. 
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then the fever and heat subside.  
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	A vein has neither heat nor fever nor pain and contains its own juice which is its proper sac and is according to the color of the body, and it begins as a small stream and grows larger. 
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either greasy or moist, and many of their colors are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a wound, that you probe and inquire first of all with any instrument called an "introducer," according to its shape or chapter which follows afterward.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiry into abscesses of us is that you take the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess. 
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the trocar, and take care in this that it does not go further. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moist matter runs out, whatever color it may have, let the patient do as I have said for other abscesses;  
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the trocar no moisture comes out, know that it is greasy, so let the patient do in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and slightly scratch it on each side, and guard the skin where it lies so that you draw it healthy with the new one. 
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, pull it out piece by piece so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the nose will return many times; 
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a piece remains and it does not bother him, apply the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and extract the wound, and put soothing things on the hot abscess, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed; 
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the nose is large, sew the two edges of the wound and treat it with what promotes flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the pulsating vein opposes you or another hastens you and applies the place of crushed vitriol, and leaves it there for two or three days, until the wound festers, and relieves the boiling of blood; 
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cut what remains in the nose.  
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of instruments for insertion, and they are of three manners: 
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small; 
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three square ones which are called “albaret”, and one which is called “breb”, and there are three manners of them:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula; 
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which we sew charms, and are made of citrine brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more, and are better tested by black lead for encircling the curves of fistula; 
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three manners: 
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the perforations. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the cannulae are of much similarity, as you see here: 
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, medium, and small; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if they are of three kinds with two curves;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if they are of three curves, and are also of three kinds; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if they are of two curves, and one curve only, and are of three kinds; 
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these with which one cuts are sharp, and there are some which do not cut more forcefully than from one side, from which one scrapes the flesh, for this reason one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; 
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these are the small hollow-handled instruments held in hand, so that the patient does not notice them when opening abscesses; 
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	Great, small, and medium, as you see; 
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And do not use them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and joints, and similar places; 
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And never make another instrument small, resembling a pestle's head, according to this shape, with which one cauterizes blood: 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it back in place which heals by joining of the veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes men's breasts swell when they begin to corrupt, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; 
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain unsightly and swollen, and those who wish to cure them, if it is necessary, must do so according to the form of this line .b. up to .g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine mixed with charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; 
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs low, and is loosened by its size as it happens with women, then make two cuts in two ribs above, through two similar incisions. 
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is held to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the largest line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; 
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then flay the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; 
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with softened cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; 
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until it fattens with marrow and grease, then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat it with an ointment suitable for it until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.
