And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, then cut it as we have said for cutting scrofula, and if the wound goes inwards, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is severed and the skin above it is sewn together, there often come abscesses, and the same thing happens with a swollen vein and an abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the one who knows cuts it when it is for the artery, the abscesses are long and straight; 
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	And when you feel it with your fingers, you feel separation;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, it appears round and fiery. 
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and at the angles or on the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore it is fitting to avoid treatment with iron, and the one who is in charge must also avoid it, and for the one who has swelling from an artery that passes beneath the skin along its length;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then work the incision as if making a notch, and neatly separate the artery from the surrounding tissues, until it is exposed. 
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle beneath it, and make it pierce through to the other side, and remove the artery with a doubled thread in two parts, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples. 
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then prick the area between the two ligatures with an introcuter until all the blood that is there comes out, and the abscess is released.  
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply a dressing that promotes healing, as long as the ligatures hold. 
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is located near the vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can grasp from the abscess along with the skin, then insert a needle beneath the area you are holding, and make it pierce through, and thread a doubled thread so that you pull it from the other side. 
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the abscess, as I have told you, with thread from one of its two sides to the two bones. 
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the thread will not come loose, put another needle through all the thread below the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull out the threads in four places. 
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess from the heart and leave what is tied. 
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a cloth softened in wine and oil on it, then give him treatments of bandages and ointments until he is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in arteries and veins, abscesses also come to nerves when they are strained, or from too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often in the shoulders and elbows and in all places where there are joints, and it is a festering sore, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in several conditions without pain. 
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is extracted formed, if the patient feels pain, and is not entirely well in the body, but below the heart; 
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor below nor above, and the one that is in joints should not be covered by iron: 
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	for fear it might cause contraction; 
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those that are on the head or forehead, make the skin with a spatula.  
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, take it with tweezers and cover it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with an awl and scarify it, then the surgeon assembles the wound with sutures, and heals it until it is healthy. 
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it occurs in bellies and nowhere else, and is a disease called “fungus” because of its resemblance to ashes, and the root is subtle, and the head large; 
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are small ones and very large ones; 
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, and had small roots, and were easily split open, and moisture ran from them immediately. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six ounces, and in operations when cutting if you see that the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and has fine roots;  
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if the cut is made with a scalpel, and there are cauteries ready. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For at the waist there often comes excessive blood flow, and if it does not stop, hurry then and cauterize. 
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient faint and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made thread of silk, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days;  
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then hold it tightly, and do not cease to pull the thread of flax until it catches the bone, and moves through it. 
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	And if the roots are large, there is fear of catching them immediately for the abdomen, but you can well catch half, then cauterize it so it does not grow back; 
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then treat the wound, and be careful not to catch the tendon which is of a reddish color and poor sense and milky appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the arm is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the swelling comes from cautery of a wound or a split in the flesh, and is on the belly and among some bowels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before it, or from windiness.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is from a rupture of the flesh and by the flow from the bowels, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens from various outlets. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when it is pressed at its hips if it rebounds, and then returns, and by chance if it is tightened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and through strenuous effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is an easy thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, but do not force it. 
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs: the abscess is large and hard, and it is fixed according to a certain quantity.  
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you look to see whether the appearance is due to the blood of an artery or vein, or windiness.  
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let the cure continue.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the bowels, then it is fitting that you instruct the patient to hold his breath, and be extended straight, then press all around the arm. 
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then command him to grasp firmly between your hands, then go around the place that you have pressed with all of the spatulum, then extend half of the abscess above at all the great one. 
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then bind it with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk tightly, and let the knot be secure. 
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work on half of the abscess stretched out over the ligature, and insert your index finger, and press the intestines. 
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught by the ligature, loosen it, and push the intestine out behind the belly.  
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the pus, take it with forceps and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein opposes you, wind carefully around it, then return to your work and take two needles, insert them with strong thread, and push the two needles around what you have already done, in a cross shape so that you pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then draw the abscess in four directions along the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles and leave the wound open until it dries, and let the dead flesh come out on its own. 
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	When you cut it when it is thin and rotten, then cure what is needed, and empty the abscess as we have said; 
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as needed, and stitch the place. 
dou chancre	Where a sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the resemblances of a sore, and how one should work by medicine, and how one should avoid the treatment with iron; 
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say that a sore spreads in the marrow, and great caution is needed in its cure, and they said the ancients that when sores are in places where one can shave them off like a sore which is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, one should remove it all when it is at the beginning; 
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, you should not approach it at all, for I have never been able to cure any. 
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	No one ever heals before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the operations, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, are that you purge the patient of black bile several times. 
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	Then make him fast if he has manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good place to perform the operation; 
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then shave your instruments or lancets, and the hair from all sides, and the bone from all sides without leaving anything; 
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and cleanse the place well with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding makes you oppose the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped. 
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with another cure until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and in what manner the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is made by medicine, and that which is cured by iron: 
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only broken; 
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch it with iron in these two cases:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and iposarche, for they are deadly things. 
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore, when you treat this type of dropsy which is called “broken” and the treatment does not work, see if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things.
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	Do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt; 
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	And if you see the patient is of strong constitution and they have only dropsy, and they are not too young nor too old, then you should proceed as follows: 
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Lay the patient straight on your hands, and have the assistant press on the belly from below, at the lowest part of the bladder. Then take the sharp-pointed spatula in this way: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	to the point, and however it is not so deep that it can reach the intestine when put in, and cannot be bleached. 
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	Then look if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines:  
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you split in its lower part three finger widths straight down above the hipbone; 
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the abdomen three finger widths.  
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is for the spleen, it should be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lies on the incision so that the excess fluids do not flow to the weak area. 
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument and push it in, and lift your hand to all the spatulas between the skin and the fascia as much as when scraping off the quantity of a fingernail or so.  
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the syfac until the spatula reaches the eighth place, and that is the place of the sharp point, then hold it firm, and push this instrument, which has the following shape: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a slender silver cane, and is made of horn or light wood, and has a small hole at the bottom. 
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	And on one side are three holes.  
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	And two on the other side, and one on another. 
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And the point is cut like a quill, and that is the shape of the incision with which scribes cut the quill: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the top is the handle so that when the instrument comes to the point, it now descends onto the instrument. 
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Empty it then halfway or a third, because if you empty more than is necessary at that time, the patient may die due to the release of his spirit from the body, or he will fall into a stupor, or approach death. 
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the void quantity of its virtue, and according to what the patient's disposition signifies, and their pulse; 
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held for the heart which pierces the pertussis that is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; 
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then start the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and treat a small amount of the point; 
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this every day, and be careful not to press while it remains but a prick of a point.  
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt the patient, and leave much of a point, let the cure be hot sand or a warm bath and sweat, and sunbathing, and have them drink plenty; 
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the cure of drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the arrow, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the severing of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without a hole in their penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary as soon as possible, so that it does not pierce all the marrow very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or make a small plug of lead, and tie it and leave it like this for three days or four and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, and urinate, and then put it back; 
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance none is needed, for the strong urine which comes will not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose openings are small, if they are treated with a clove of garlic, as we have said, it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the passage in their place are wretched, for none are born who have a passage at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up; 
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come up to the urethra, and this is a bad illness. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then they extend the head of the penis and the foreskin as the size of a quill, so that the hole pierces in the middle, as it should be; 
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And beware of the flow of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, use a styptic to stop the bleeding, and dress the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the boils of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times these pustules come on the penis, and they are an unsightly appearance of flesh; 
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malignant and benign ones; 
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	it is necessary that you take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and clean them all, then put softened cotton with Egyptian ointment on top; 
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dress it with diachylon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of a foul color and discharging, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have caught it, and if the albathed is at the top of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the albathed which is inside first. 
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when it is soldered, so the cure is outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you cure it together, if the head of the penis is not well secured so that it is not pierced, and blackness and corruption comes in its penis and groin; 
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	it is necessary to cut away everything that is black and corrupted, then bind it with a plaster of honey and flour which is made of pomegranate rind and vinegar, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood comes, then apply the crescent cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	Cauteries help in two ways together: 
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	That is to say, in the stopping of blood, and in corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is fitting that you apply or insert into the penis a cane of lead, and have the patient urinate through it.  
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hairs grow around the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, then it is fitting that you burn it off with a heated instrument, so that the bonds are loosened and the head of the penis is freed on all sides. 
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if this is a difficult thing to do, it is fitting that you burn it off with a spatula at some point on the head of the penis and on the skin. 
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then carefully separate them between, and apply a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water so that it does not burn again. 
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a loosening of continuity like the other wounds; 
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	However, when we perform this work of our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest for salvation. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I want most masters and surgeons who performed circumcision to do it in one go, with force, and with a single incision; 
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if the heart failed because there are two layers, and perhaps one cuts above and leaves the one below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Here it is necessary to cut again, and there is double pain, and for healing which is in two layers, the tip of the member is not well secured. 
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	And for the healing of one layer, perhaps the iron slips and spoils the work, and many times are born so they do not need healing and I want it this way. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the cleansing which is done with all the force of the thread I have found the benefit of experience for the force cuts precisely as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut equally in a straight line. 
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	But let the threads be well twisted around the leather;  
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	And the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if they understand, that you are only doing it to tie the thread around the penis, and then you can reassure them in all the ways you can. 
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then let it come out between your hands straight, and hold the force between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments. 
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then put your hand on the penis and blow or breathe on it, and pull it up until the head of the penis is in. 
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then cleanse it well of the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the place with a doubled thread, then tie it below the penis at the other tie. 
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it with your second finger to the pouch and the index finger, and grasp between the two ligatures, then lift the heart quickly from above and treat the head of the penis. 
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood run drop by drop, for that is the best. 
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on top and on top of the powder I drape it with a half of a cooked egg tempered with rose water, confit with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with another cure as long as it is healed.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of forces in the world is this: 
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two cheeks should be held and sharp, and the cheeks should also be as large as the handle equally.  
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of the world is when the hearts inside flee at the incision. 
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, just as pus forms an abscess; 
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	And the cap similarly, and if you cannot hold it at your finger, then take tongs and hold the cap. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they exceed three days, and that which is beneath the foreskin is swollen, then leave it until the abscess under the foreskin is calmed, and lightly scrape it. 
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If the cap can be moved as you are able, and take care of the part of the foreskin, for it will do no harm.  
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Then cure the place of things within the wound with powder as we have said in our treatise on powders, and if the cap is too tight and goes up, it will do no harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore cure it, as we have said, until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	Concerning the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine can be due to stones, or congealed blood, or a bowel obstruction, or a dead fetus, or similar things, as we have said in the division. 
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone at the neck of the bladder, then it is appropriate for the patient to be bent over on his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And his feet should be placed on his back and he should stretch out his belly above his back, and restrain the patient from moving as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	Then the neck of the bladder is constricted to force out the stone above so that the urine can be released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient is in great pain, then you must administer an extraction using an instrument called a “syringe,” which has this form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	And it should be of finely wrought silver, light as a bird's feather. 
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And the handle should be a palm and a half long, and fine at the top. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of removing urine is this: you take a doubled thread and tie a piece of wool or cotton to the top, and insert the top of the thread into the syringe;  
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess wool and insert it up to the top of the syringe. Then grease the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water;  
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the buttocks; 
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then insert the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder and feel the patient's urine flow into the empty vessel and this is not done according to this order unless the guide where it goes is crooked. 
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then extend the thread to all the wool bit by bit and the urine follows the wool then extract it and make the urine flow. 
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And start the syringe again until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved.  
des maladies de la vessie	of the illnesses of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorches or blood comes to the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see sharp waters and medicines distilled, then do it with all the instrument which is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed and if it has three openings: 
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side and one on the other as you see.
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	And the leaves should be cut so that the medicine shortens it well without addition, if one can draw out the moisture and insert it when needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	And when you see your medicines going into the bladder put the head of the catheter in the moisture and draw it out with what is inside. 
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you treat the moisture at the joint, and then firmly bind the limb; 
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	The moisture will enter the limb, and will come to the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it; 
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	And this is the form of a subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder:  
si est ci:	This is it: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is made of silver or pewter, and the head is higher;  
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	And below at its side where the linen string is attached; 
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	Then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture which you saw used to enema the bladder into it, then tie it between the two breasts with a good strong string doubled over, and heat the whole thing on the fire;  
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then insert the head of the enema into the urethra, and hold your hand on the bladder to keep all the moisture flowing until the patient feels that the moisture has arrived in the bladder; 
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it round about. 
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then thread a strong cord through these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a ball, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it to the instrument. 
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already said in the division the manners of stone, and its extraction together with medicines. 
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And I have said the difference between a stone lodged in the reins and all its signs, and in what kind of stone one should operate with a cut. 
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the sharp point of the stone resembles the point of a needle in its subtlety. 
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	And it opens wide and grates on the patient's penis, and penetrates it many times, and then it twists. 
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	And many of these points are dissolved;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	And healing is easy for children until they are four years old, and it is very painful in older people, and is in the middle for those who are between youth and old age. 
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	And the treatment is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by enema, to draw out all the slime that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet and push them down so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and it comes out sometimes from the top. 
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your hands evenly balanced, and let his hands be under his thighs so that his bladder is entirely inclined downwards. 
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then grasp it and touch it inside. 
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut upon the stone.  
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not move at all when touched, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a woman, or your middle finger if the patient is a young man; 
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and insert it into his fundament and grasp the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bind it at the neck of the bladder. 
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press upon your finger and insert it to where you see you must cut.  
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand and tell him to extend the testicles upwards with his right hand, and to remove the skin that is below the testicles in the area where the incision will be made.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then he thrusts the spatulate instrument cutting, of which this is the form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And he makes an incision between what is between the thighs and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; 
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and it should be straight above the stone, and your two hands should be right there at the fundament, and let the waist be wide externally and narrow internally, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; 
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by chance, if the hand that is at the fundament presses so that it jumps out without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there are stones which have angles and margins: 
si est griés a issir;	if it is grated to come out;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and there are some which are underneath, resembling a bean and round, of which the exit is easy. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Therefore when there are angles and a margin, make the size greater. 
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	And if it does not come out, it is fitting that you extract it with tongs which are also like a file at the head, in order to pull out the stone so that it does not escape. 
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	Or you insert below it a subtle instrument bent at the head; 
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	And if you cannot introduce it thus, enlarge the hole a little, and if the stone is not softened, extract it with vitriol. 
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there are more than one stones, insert the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then those on top, then force it through and the small ones afterwards if there are several.  
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must sew it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient: 
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	Either he dies, or his urine comes out immediately because the veins cannot join together.  
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	But nevertheless, strive to draw it out or break it apart with forceps, so that you draw it out piece by piece. 
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	And when you have completed your work, apply to the wound frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, draw it out, and put on top a cloth softened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess. 
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then put the patient back on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.  
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if it rises very well in a place of oil and water, then cure it with diachylon ointment and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if abscesses come into the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and urine is retained by this, which is known in part to flow without a jump along with the urine. 
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then put your finger in the wound and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and rot it.  
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound with a sharp point and a needle and thread, and help it in all the ways you know, until it is healed; 
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that every hour that you treat it, you bind the two thighs together, and apply the medicines on the spot. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is lodged in the urethra, and stuck there, and the urine cannot pass;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the cure that I have just mentioned is done, then you are excused from cutting many times because of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron forceps according to this shape and let it have three angles fixed in the fire:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; 
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then insert the borer into the penis lightly, until it reaches the stone; 
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	And turn the borer in your hand on the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone through to the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If urine comes soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is soon broken and jumps out with the urine, the patient is cured.  
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread under the stone and another above it, then cut the penis where the stone is between the two threads, then extract it forcefully, and untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound.  
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It can happen that a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens sometimes, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: 
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	One is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; 
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to reveal herself naked, especially when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is such that by chance one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; 
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth manner is such that the stone of the woman is more deeply set than the stone of the man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, it is fitting that you take a midwife well-knowing, and one rarely finds her, and if you do not find her, do not cast in a subtle mirror; 
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present a midwife well-versed in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquiry into the stone; 
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: 
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is fitting for her to put her finger or foundation and seek the stone; 
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, she should constrain it below her finger, and recommend that she put her finger or the patient's hand, and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves it quickly from the entrance of the bladder to below, as long as it comes to the root of the thigh; 
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then she presses on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it is most easily moved, and feels the stone in that part;  
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and does not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the size be at first small; 
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then put the knife in the size, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound as much as the stone can come out forcefully, and know that there are many kinds of stones: 
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	This is to know, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have veins. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the resemblances to recognize the outcome
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the vein goes away, put powdered vitriol on it, and hold it for an hour until the vein is extinguished. 
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	Then return to your work while the stone is strong, and have the instruments that I told you about for extracting the stone from men to help you in your work. 
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	And if the vein goes away and it is an artery that is cut, put powder on the area and bind it with bandages and cloths, and do not start again that day, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, for fear the patient might die. 
puis cure la plaie.	Then treat the wound.  
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the pain subsides, you may return to your work, as long as the stone remains hard.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Ramices aqueous is nothing other than an accumulation of moisture or white phlegm, which is below the heart of the testicles and contains sperm.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac," and never properly in the cloth of an egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; 
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the skin under the white syfac that we have said; 
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this did not occur to us.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this branch is so weak that it comes to the joints, and is spread throughout the matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never if it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: 
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	it is colored declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; 
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this gathering, for if it is white syfac as we have said, it is a boil on the testicles; the sore is long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the testicles, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the actual cloth, the abscess will return with a portion of the egg, and for this reason it is thought that it is another egg. 
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white sinew, then one feels it well. 
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Therefore, when you see that you know the color of the moisture, then try all the instruments, of which the form is described above. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this which comes after the introducer, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cauterize it with iron, it is fitting that the patient be purged according to our power and the fullness of his body. 
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	Then place him on his back, on something a bit high, and put many cloths under him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	Then sit on his left, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the instrument to one of the two ribs near the testicles.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the scalpel sharp and cut the skin of the testicles among them along the length down to the knife's point and let your incision be perfectly straight in dividing the skin of the testicles until white flesh, and flay it subtly according to the poor man. 
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the white flesh clear with a sharp large hole and extract all the pus, and then put your ointments and raise the white flesh up. 
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	And do not touch the heart of the testicles, but only the white flesh.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cut all or in parts immediately its side subtly, so that if you do not cut it wisely, the pus will return. 
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	And if the testicle jumps out during your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the white flesh.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then join the two lips of the heart of the testicles with a suture, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find that the egg is corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspensory, doubting the flow of blood. 
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cut the colon at all the suspensory points, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the sharp is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches.  
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	If you cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound linen moistened in rose oil. 
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put another linen moistened in wine and oil, and put it on the two cuts, and put doubled cloths on top, and tie them up according to this form. 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with shredded linen according to this appearance, and they are assembled by stitching in the throat of the breeches, and one of the ends takes hold on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part by the handle. 
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two chiefs on the two angles, and let all the restraint be assembled in the loop of the arm; 
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this branch of the cautery medicated in place of an iron blade, but rather you take a delicate surgical cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we have said, so that the white fascia containing the nerve is exposed. 
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that fascia with it, and flay it with this delicate hot cautery: 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut in all the ways you can, until you have completely eradicated it.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and take care that the fire does not touch the testicle; 
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	And know that this work is safer;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and easier to manage bleeding, and milder than the operations of incision. 
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if anything opposes you, whether an abscess or discharge of blood or something else, then treat what opposes you, according to what has been said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horribleness, then make a small perforation as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs we have said that the aqueous humor is there, then have the patient sit on a raised seat; 
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess at the bottom part across the whole width, and make the perforation as long as the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the opening be wide so that all the humor can flow out; 
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the spot and bind it, and let the remaining humor flow out, then treat it until the wound is healed; 
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not let the pus out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you put a feather in it or an instrument with which one treats the dropsy, of which the shape is mentioned before; 
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the sore, and know that the pus will return, and gather after six months or so; and when it is gathered as before, then the patient will spend his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this branch there are many positions out of fear, for which it seems to me better to leave it. 
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the likenesses of the abscess.  
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come on the body, and likewise on the buttocks; 
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is by many instances.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to know by excess of sharp and bitter humor, which is spread to the joints, or from impact. 
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	And the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; 
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And there is no pain found, and it is a grievous abscess; 
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance there are some abscesses that are gray, porous and pierced, and of a dark color, and sometimes it comes from a new artery or swelling of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a new artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers. 
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And it is not advisable that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is made from swelling of a vein is known by its disposition upon the touch of the fingers and one can well make an incision upon this type and upon others. 
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the heart of the onions, then lift up the egg white, and draw it forth from the white sinew, and deliver the suspender from all parts of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg white is already cooked with these new things, then it is fitting that you draw out the egg white, and cut it. 
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is attached to the sinew, or in those that are inside the vessels, then it is fitting that you deliver all of that membrane, and cut it roundly.  
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is behind or elsewhere, it is necessary that you cut all of it and extract the egg as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess wrapped in an envelope resembling a poppy seed pod, with the softening of onions, and the patient groans when he goes. 
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the treatment of this illness is just as fearful as the one before, and nonetheless we will tell you its work, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is fitting that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then put the suspensory from his testicles down to your thighs, to all the vessels that are near the penis, and tie them tightly. 
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then take a sharp scalpel and cut through the vessels in a wide area until they are exposed, then flay from each side as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; 
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then he puts in a needle with a doubled thread and ties it to the first place where the vein came out, and ties it straight across to the other end; 
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then he cuts them in the middle straight according to the length of the body, and draws out the corrupted humors;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then heals the wound as the others where we inject a bowel so that no vessel bursts that nourishes one of the testicles;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by this no harm comes and if all the vessels come into view then it is necessary to draw the veins at all the vessels 
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the bone does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels and they dry up and cannot be helped 
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the facial bone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this branch is by the section which comes or arises on the belly in the part of the groin so that the intestines descend from this rupture to one of the veins 
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is either at the groin or from the extension of it and these two manners come from many causes 
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	either from a blow, or a jump, or a struggle, or the lifting of something heavy and by similar things 
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the groin are that it happens little by little over a long time and does not come suddenly
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the abscess is equalized up to the fundament, so that the pus follows the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of the fistula, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and there are various abscesses appearing underneath the skin nearby, and it is due to the exit of the intestine and the body's defenses against the fistula.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never remove the intestines with the entrails, and it is retained there, and causes great pain to be suffered by the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments due to fear, for which it is advisable to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the way of working is such that you instruct the patient to massage the intestines with his hand inside the wound, if he can enter;
