Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a striking of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt a hot abscess: 
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	If it bleeds quickly from the cephalic vein itself, if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side of the injured part. 
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And forbid the patient from eating rich food and large meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not bleed, let his food be reduced, and do not drink wine, nor eat meat. 
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And place on the wound, if an abscess seems to be coming, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine. 
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh and bleeding freely, and not moved by air, powder, which I will mention a little later. 
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has already moved it, put on some ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by bandages, then stitch them together, as I will say for abdominal wounds, using sutures.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to bone, and it can, and it does not hold except by a point, then sew it. 
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten flesh that does not reach the bone, then sew up all the rotted part and cut it out, then treat it.  
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if it has an artery or vein in the wound that is bleeding and cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with thread. 
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And put this powder on it so that it heals as if the fire had moved it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the way of the powder is: 
pren encens une partie;	Take frankincense one part; 
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts; 
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	quicklime three parts, and powder it subtly, and apply it to the wound, and remove it when it burns well and joins with all its blood; 
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, and leave it without being unbound, unless it swells;  
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do this with chalk alone, when one does not have incense nor dragon's blood, but that the fire has heated the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has already moved the wound, do not put this powder on it at all; 
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digested ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it flows well; 
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure other cures until he is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with subtle pincers; 
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you here after about the fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves in the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment, and do not put anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; 
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuity is with the brain, which is the highest member; 
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be below, such as chamomile washed in clear water, and mixed with rose oil, and chamomile washed also in clear water, and other stones of the mine according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is swollen and full of pus, then pierce it lower. 
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut and blood flows, then bind it, and tie it, and cautery is necessary. 
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is kept by which the meat goes, then sew the heart onto the cane of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape. 
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then remove carefully and leave it for a few days, then treat it with dry dressings until it is healed. 
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then cauterize it. 
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot obtain, leave them until the wound rots, is cleansed, and its exit is aligned.  
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on top of the powder that I have mentioned. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a cut from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if air escapes when the patient breathes. 
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Then you know the wound is mortal; 
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder on it for the first hour, nor bind it so that the blood does not cease flowing freely, return to the heart, and kill the patient. 
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But apply an attractive ointment and bind it twice a day. 
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	And if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck up moisture and let the patient sleep on the wound for three, four, or more days.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there comes no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor dislocations of the bone; 
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it with bandages and other treatments, until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, then know that there is a fistula; 
si la cure si com on doit.	if the cure is as it should be. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether on the leg or the back, treat it as you would any other wound in that location; 
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, suture it; 
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, treat it with powder, and if it has penetrated the bone and shattered pieces, clean the wound and remove any foreign objects if they are loose; 
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not mature, let the wound fester, so that extraction is easier. 
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other limbs, judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	For a rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great, medium and small; 
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, by which entry of others (is possible); 
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because one puts the intestines back in more easily if one does not put them back hot by hot; 
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell quickly when they feel cold and enter more easily, and therefore it is better to mend the middle-sized wound because one can move the intestine to its place better than the others. 
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is according to four manners: 
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds. 
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And all the same they are more fitting with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is outside, and it is an easy matter to put it back in, this can be done in one of two ways. 
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen because of the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in two ways: 
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Soak a sponge or a soft cloth in hot water only, or you can cook in hot water squinant and cypress and spikenard, and apply to the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never make this wine restraining, and it is better to give alone for disentanglement. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestines with sharp or high and bad things that are cooked, for by this is alleviated the entrance to little. 
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it cannot enter, then make a small wound with an instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; 
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is better than cutting, that no one should cut without great necessity.  
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And these are the instruments for splitting it: 
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut inside in the curve and do not remove it, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine has come out, if you put it back in according to its natural form in its proper place, if you have the power, because this is worth a lot.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part below the belly, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; 
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and the breast higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture from the belly is in one of the two sides then put your understanding in this way that the injured side be higher than the other. 
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is fitting to administer what I say in large and small wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds put what appears to you, then have between your hands a minister gentle who holds all the rupture in his hand, and brings together the lips. 
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a half a space, and there you put in a needle where it has a good strong thread. 
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the sinew, which is beneath the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two edges of the sinew four together. 
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then strain a double thread onto the needle in two parts, then bring together the two sides of the wound evenly, and then leave one finger's space, and insert another needle. 
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the two threads as you did with the first needle, and do not cease doing this according to what you need needles for, until the whole wound is restrained.  
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium-sized, between subtle and thick, for subtle needles pierce all the flesh, and those too thick cannot enter well.  
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore it is fitting that they should be medium-sized. 
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And it is not fitting to drive the needles too far beyond the flesh and skin so that they pierce and open the wound before the suturing. 
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then tie the sides of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and apply bandages or cloths to the sides of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is sutured.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it uses one needle or two. 
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and it consists of assembling the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the sinew together with one needle having a strong medium-sized thread. 
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have pierced all these sides together, pull the needle back to where you started, in the manner one sews cloths. 
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And leave a space between each stitch the width of two grains of pepper.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch heals a man, and I sewed a wound on a man's belly, who had been cut by a knife, the wound was more than a handspan large and the intestines protruded two handspans, and the wound was in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I put the intestine back in place after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound healed until the 15th day, and I cared for it, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they thought he would die, and it was a miracle. 
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine. 
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put nothing more on the wound than old cotton twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching.
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and push it through from the far side to the near side. 
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the flesh straight through, take the thread or twine or whatever you have put the needle through and make it pierce from the other side from the inside out.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this stitch is that you sew just as furriers sew furs, and that you leave the thread once on one side and pick it up again on the other, until the entire stitch is complete. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of suturing, which Galen properly calls, is as follows: they bring the two parts together naturally and apply one end of the silk to the other end in this manner.  
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle or silk thread close by and make it pass through that place only, leaving the two ends of the silk. 
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle and make it pass through from the outer part to the inner part, along with the two ends of the silk. 
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then make both pass from the outer part to the inner part, in two other silk threads that are on the other side.  
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the simplest way of suturing and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen said these words, and some confirm it, that one must sew the abdomen with two needles, each with thread. 
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must put a needle from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew straps. 
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than those of other places in the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of the other wounds: 
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, in such a way that the artery has moved it, then put back the intestine, and the seam. 
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then put on charred charcoal powder, and if the artery has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound swells. 
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And stitch the thread, and weld the sinew, and the muscle.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed.  
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have medicines, as soon as it begins to boil put old cotton on it, and move it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicine in several situations unless the wounds are complex.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound might cause a communal infection with principal members, it is fitting that you moisten linen lightly in tempered oil, or rose oil, and place it around the wounds, and under the armpits. 
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then enemas of warm black wine, and similarly if the putrefaction reaches the intestines. 
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small intestine. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the arrangement of its veins, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the splinter jumps from the wound, put it back as you would the intestines, while it is fresh. 
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has become green or black, you must bind the black area so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries. 
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut what is between the ligature and place the two ends hanging down from the part below the wound until it falls out to ease extraction when the splinter comes out, and the wound heals. 
de la routure dou boueil	from a fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are round and the wound is small, some men can restore them, for I have seen a man who was wounded in the belly by a spear; 
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was excretion and flatulence; 
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I have put a cure according to what I could, and did not stop trying to refine it until he was healed, and his wounds were sutured. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sutured, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his belly; 
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he did not have any pain, but remained in better condition, and ate and drank;  
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in a certain way: 
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take threads of large size, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened its mouth, place it upon the two lips so that it tightens its mouth above; 
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut the thread's end, and this stays so that it cannot loosen, then place another thread afterward in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; 
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the hair burns in the intestine and no harm comes to the patient, then one can tie the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal. 
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the end of this intestine thread that is well frayed, and then tie to the end of this thread a fine linen thread twisted, then put the thread in the needle and sew the intestine and rejoin it at the tear. 
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this way of sewing is nothing but according to the way of trust and hope;  
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal folds, there is no remedy or safety except subtlety.  
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it gets old, is called universally "fistula," and the same when it is healed and drawn inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the greenness of a hard and white knot where there is no pain felt, and it rises as high as the feather of a bird. 
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes it jumps clear thin, and other times thick. 
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes it bursts forth, and other times enough. 
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	And as I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, any wound that is not healed and there is no flesh, it only flows by one of nine causes: 
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	That is to say, by the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	Or by its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	Or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Or because there is too much pus; 
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Or the wound is infected and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	Or the medicine is not good in the treatment; 
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	Or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where by its property in the region digestion is slow, and sensation is late, and it swells naturally; 
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones: 
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I make you know the cure of fistula which is made by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all the limbs of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the diaphragm, or the intestines, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; 
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it happens that it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil, and ignorance; 
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have mentioned, and you are confident of the cure, and you see it known, then take a tent of iron or of bronze, if the fistula is straight, if the other. 
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is crooked, then make a tent of lead, for lead bends and conforms to the crook. 
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well enclose it with tents, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture passes from one opening to another and cleanses it. 
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then carefully bleed it to your power, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is well drawn out, and inquire well from the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it. 
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the putrefaction and the corrupted flesh that are inside; 
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in the right place, it is necessary that you cut deeply, as much as you can, then put soft tents soaked in hot medicine, and push them to the bottom of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; 
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then apply ointments that regenerate healthy flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not hinder you or the main limbs, as we have said; 
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, remove all the corruption until it is gone, then treat the surrounding flesh as needed until it is healed. 
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not healed and returns as before, know that you have not gone far enough. 
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If uncovered and sought until you reach the bottom, remove all corruption, then restore the area.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is healed thus, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; 
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature. 
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there is a small corrupted bone and you can remove it with forceps, extract it with an appropriate instrument for this purpose. If there are many bones, remove them all, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, then grasp both moisture and flesh, and free the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put something promoting decay on the wound, and leave it until the flesh is rotted around the bones, and then you will remove the bones more easily; 
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then allow only the corruption until the blackness is all removed, then restore the wound; 
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part corrupted and it reaches the marrow of the bone;  
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then you must saw and cut all the way to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed together; 
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man of about thirty years who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the humors came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and he had no reason to open. 
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But his doctors, in their folly, worked so much on the abscess that they opened it and corroded a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many holes that all flowed with pus and moisture from the body. 
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no one who knew anything about surgery, until I was called to see him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed from the holes in large quantities. 
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And his young body was becoming red and had a yellow color.  
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I stuck a tent into one of these holes, and then I encircled all the holes, and I found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hastened therefore, and cut into one of the pores until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption was coming to the bone inside. 
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away what appeared to me to be the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except that which I removed; 
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with hot medicines for a long time, and could not solder it; 
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and I scraped it, and then removed it, and struggled to solder the place. 
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's breadth of the bone, and treated it thoroughly to its entire marrow, then I restored it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it was healed and joined quickly, and there was no need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation often bled, but it was healed completely, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was of good disposition and had no harm nor contrary of any kind, neither at coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be treated in this manner: 
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take a bandage and bind it to the head of the bone that appears, and order someone to extend it upwards; 
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another bandage of wool larger than the first bandage and tie it on the flesh that is below the bone, and extend the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh on the place where you wish to sew, so that the thread does not injure the flesh; 
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot coal or a wooden board below the bone to help cook the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to treat as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to treat again another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and it does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then lay bare all the flesh. 
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put the ember underneath, and then treat from one part to the other the corruption, and let the treatment be as long as the corruption, one finger's breadth, as we have said. 
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and treat the bone where it holds on the other side.  
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut them. 
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the corruption is in a finger of the hand or a toe, that is very serious, but nevertheless you must inquire into this corrosion, how it appears to you. 
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but make sure that the vein or nerve does not oppose you. 
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And know that the incisors and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness. 
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And therefore it is fitting to prepare an instrument for each type of work; 
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of illnesses. 
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	Therefore prepare the instrument you need according to what is fitting. 
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can dislocate either from internal causes or external causes; 
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated the corruption with medicine, and it does not improve, then it is necessary to cut that limb up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes death, or from the greater malice of losing the limb. 
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness comes the corruption of member to member, and takes hold throughout the body. 
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you are bitten by a viper, and if it is by the sting of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion or an adder and similar creatures, if the corruption is at the head of the wound, cut it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm; 
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, cut it at the elbow; 
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there are no remedies except for the quantity of its venom. 
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do the same when the corruption comes or the foot: 
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then the cup after the other joint; 
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cup the whole foot; 
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, then cup at the knee joint; 
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die;  
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the way to cup or sew the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister's bandage downwards, and another minister's bandage upwards, and you cut the flesh that is between the two bandages at a span wide, as long as the bone is uncovered; 
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cup or sew, and put on each side a linen cloth so that the sewing does not touch the healthy area, and causes the patient other injury and abscesses. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding comes while you work, quickly cauterize the area or apply some restraining powders. 
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and care for it until it is healed. 
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to a man in his own foot: 
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He developed a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corruption first came in the back of his foot until it spread throughout his entire foot. 
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he immediately hastened to cover his foot and it was healed. 
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And a long time after, the corruption returned to the back of his hand. He came to me and I applied reparative things to him after cleansing his body, but I could not stop the corruption.  
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to hold his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of recovering the substance. 
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if I cut his hand, he would not die, because the strength of the man was weak. 
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he completely despaired, and returned to his land, and hastened to grasp his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I only relate this story because one may do something else if needed. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in the flesh, and lasts so long that it causes a large gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it breaks open and bursts, and the pus escapes, and the wound remains hollow, like some vessels. 
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin on top is as delicate as a linen cloth, and does not reach to the bone or to the nerve, and this kind of illness is called "healthy" and is not called "fistula". 
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so lengthened that it comes to the bone quite clearly, it is called a "fistula" 
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and if the skin is so that you can peel back all around it, and even when it is thin, like a cloth; 
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not become foul because of its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you believe that the skin will burn, and the corruption is not quite clear, and the skin is thick like leather, then treat it with an enema as follows: 
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the bowels are large and the belly that comes from it has a foul odor, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made as follows: 
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take alum, oil and litharge, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey. 
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take some according to your need, and make it with vinegar and honey, and apply it as an enema on the breast, and extract the pus. 
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And let the medicine remain for two hours, then remove it while squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times until the breast is softened and the pus is removed. 
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And at no time apply an enema of vinegar ash when this medicine is not present, and take ashes from grapevine wood, pour vinegar on top, then strain it and apply as an enema until you know that the breast is well cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the vinegar ash, then apply an enema of vinegar and honey or a little bit of powdered litharge. 
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Where you cleanse it with honey and mead wine, so that the honey has the property of purifying and cleansing, and the wine makes the body healthy; 
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this, and you are confident that the breast is well purified, then cleanse it with something that produces flesh in it, and take a plaster that draws out moisture, and make it with rose oil and wine; 
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Or you cleanse it with certain medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or treat the ointments; 
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the opening of the breast is small and the nozzle of the clyster cannot enter, widen it a little with an iron tool, and put in a tent made of Egyptian ointment or basil ointment until it is enlarged. 
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too large, sew it up and leave only the place where the clyster can enter; and if the opening that leads to the bowels is above, make the cut lower than where it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the belly is perfect, do not allow flesh to grow. 
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, arrange it in such a way that the belly descends to the lowest place it is; for when the belly is perfect, do not allow flesh to grow and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, arrange it in this manner: 
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	Let the belly descend slightly, and do not leave any of the belly. 
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take consolidating medicines to put on the healthy flesh, and spread them on a linen cloth that covers all the flesh;  
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then cover as firmly as possible the opening of the breast so that it is wider than the first, and spread ointment softly on the other cloth according to the size of the opening, and put it on the opening of the flesh to straighten the belly, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; 
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is outside the breastbone opening removes often to remove the bowels and know what runs from the bowels whether it is venom or pus or enough, whether digested or undigested. 
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	And take notice whether the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in some way and you see the nature that jumps up on the breastbone opening, know that the breasts are already healing and health approaches. 
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then untie it in the morning or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, if you change another cloth and renew the ointment.  
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast swells with undigested food after many days, know that the breast does not air out.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair of health at all, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose wounds heal slowly, and those who do the opposite. 
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if undigested bowels jump from the breast after many days, know that the breasts are not healing. 
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breasts are slow to heal and are elongated, then apply drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as ointment diafinit, for it has a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; 
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take ointment diafinit, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance; 
puis le confit et en use;	Then boil it and use it; 
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and the same honey thickened by cooking will be better when diafinit ointments are not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey when it is off the fire; 
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	then make it into a paste and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer aristolochia longa and roots of orris, which are also like flour of vetch and centaury; 
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in use of simples or compounds: 
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	crush them, and make a powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is thoroughly embedded, and makes an impression in the bone, or hard limbs, or limbs; 
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the fistula cure, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A felon is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger or toe, or by chance arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is inflamed, and no heed is paid to it, then it comes to an abscess, runs and drains pus so much that it runs to the root of the nail, and by chance runs all.  
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And corrosion comes to the bone, until a foul odor appears, and the flesh around it becomes wide, and the color is dark red. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluous flesh that remains from the wound, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is of great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy; 
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to grow in, and there is a wound, then you should place a wedge under the nail that points at the flesh, lift it up high, and cut away this flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicines that are burning and corrosive to remove all of it; 
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure the injury with ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut and treat harshly, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; 
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the flesh corrupting, cut it in a line as previously described, then treat it until it is healed; 
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is fierce, and swollen, and it feels great pain, then you must first heal it. 
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail with a sharp instrument, cutting across it, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain.  
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, apply something soothing on top. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two nails that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a part where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some us of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born in any part of the bone do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the bone may move. 
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The incision for one who is fleshy should be light, in a half manner.
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide instrument. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those who are born at the root of the joint are painful to treat.
si te tien dou coper.	You must hold them in order to cut them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born or must be delivered soon, it is fitting that you cut the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone in a manner suitable for this, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The soldering which comes to the two bones together comes by birth or by soldering of a wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is fitting that you copy this suture so that it may repair according to its natural forms. 
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two soft cloths or bandages soaked in rose oil so that they do not fuse together.  
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you may put it between two thin pieces of lead until the edges are fused together as it should be. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a suture comes to any of its fingers with the palm, treat that suture as it should be.
des vils	of old
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large vessels wrapped full of melancholy superfluities which come from various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to him several times purging of bile, and then the juice of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment with iron is according to two methods:  
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is where they are cauterized and strong black blood is drawn out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other method is that you tie off the vein and treat it thoroughly.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The waist is set according to this manner: 
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First raise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thigh is softened, then strain the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; 
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then let and draw strong black blood from it with your hand, from one side to the other, until as much blood has issued as the strength of the patient can bear; 
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it up and instruct him to abstain from meats containing black coal;  
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full and hurt the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The raising of it is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell; 
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then apply it to the vein for as long as from the top of the knee or in the part below the ankle; 
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply the leather to the incision and flay the vein on each side until it appears when touched; 
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the leather it also appears white like a rope;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then put the vein under it as long as it is raised from the leather, and then lightly bind it to the incision, then apply it to another place above for three days; 
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then flay the leather on the vein until it appears, then lift it with a razor as you did, and bind it to another incision as you did first; 
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then apply another cut, or several if you need them, then lift it and apply it to the toe, then train and lift it up to the second cut; 
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it by degrees, until it is all out, then the cup. 
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot draw it out and lift it, put a strong doubled needle through the whole thing, tie it, and pull it, and put it below the thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out. 
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And be careful that it does not break off, for if it breaks off, one cannot draw it out or lift it, and harm comes to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have drawn it all out, put moistened wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the site of the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the bone is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not break it. 
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein if it is curved and does not cut, then it will cut the vein. 
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is of a large curve, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be large as we have said, and this is the form: 
de la voinne civile	from the vein civil
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture. 
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the putrefaction that comes below the skin, as snakes and worms come within the body, you will find it between the skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder joint opens, it is necessary that you wrap around it a piece of linen from three and a half to four inches, tie it, and leave the linen hanging on the leg, and every time it becomes wet, you wrap it again in the linen and tie it. 
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all out.
