car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will return into the flesh, and cause an abscess and putrefaction or elsewhere, and bad sickness. 
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for this reason it is necessary that it be treated bit by bit until the end, and nothing remain on or in the flesh. 
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And it sometimes happens that this vein, when treated, is V palms long or X, and one man once came to me to whom it issued from X palms in length, and when you cut it, it bursts I rays or perforations, and pierce it through to the bottom so that all comes out. 
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter which is inside be emptied, and apply to the place healing medicines that prevent putrefaction any day, then treat it as abscesses.  
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never put your hand on this vein unless it is open at the joint of the foot or leg, and it comes out with many pores, from which blood jumps. 
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Therefore cure it as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This ailment is called in our land “ox disease” because it often occurs in oxen and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh and travels throughout the body going up and down, and he feels it well from limb to limb as long as it runs under the skin where it goes, and jumps hard.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is engendered by the corruption of certain humors, just as worms and snakes and lampreys and roundworms in the belly come. 
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And there is doubt about its harmfulness because when it travels through the body and rises to the head and enters the eye by chance, it destroys the eye. 
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cleansed and milked, one cannot know that except when it goes: 
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore, it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong tight ligature, then cut it above and milk it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies;  
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs the eye, as we have said; 
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the eye, remove the eyebrow below it, then cut it above and milk it out;  
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and one must make the patient use cleansing of the body with dissolving medicines for corrupting bad humors, and beware of meats that cause putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member; 
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; 
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and a little while after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm to her shoulder, faster than anything else, like living silver when it cuts from one place to another; 
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place and settled in her shoulder, and then a little while after it ran throughout her whole body, until it reached the other arm;  
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning again around her body, just as I saw it. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had pain move from one place to another, but I had never seen it like this, as I saw it in the woman; 
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and uncovered veins, and because of that appeared this constrained windiness. 
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and have moist bodies and filled veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this illness being cured and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, immediately apply a bandage above and below, and then bind it tightly until that constrained windiness in the place has gone out. 
et cauterize le leu;	And cauterize the place; 
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it in your own eyes, so the cure of those who drive out windinesses, such as fetid pills, and serpentaria pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse according to their appearance and according to the places of the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are some that have large points, small ones, shaved ones, and sewn ones. 
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those where there are pieces; 
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which falls in any member falls according to two manners: 
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	where it falls in a principal member such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the signs of death which I will tell you hereafter appear to you: 
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	it is fitting that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in several ways;  
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these evil signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it and care for the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone and cuts through the dura mater which is on top of the brain is when there is dimness and drowsiness and dizziness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; 
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it lacks strength from the nostrils, or the ears; 
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it loses speech and voice; 
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and pus leaps from the wound, white in appearance, resembling a poultice, and also leaps like burning charcoal; 
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, then hold back from treatment, and treat the arrow only if it is not embedded.  
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow when it strikes or pierces are that it is near the left breast, and also feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; 
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and brings forth black blood, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: 
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without doubt that death approaches.  
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has not been properly removed is that without any discharge of pus it jumps from the wound and the throat swells, and the patient changes color and sighs deeply and desires cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow strikes in the covering of the buttock, it is below the small ribs; 
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and gives great pain and great sorrow and sighs; 
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves all the members of the shoulders. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach or intestines, by chance some undigested flesh may leap from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces or lodges in the belly, and does not pass through the intestines, there is no hope of a cure, nor of extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and the urine jumps out and goes away, and the patient feels great pain: 
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and thigh and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous as I will tell you what happened to me so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell or pierced at the root of the nose: 
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and drew it out on the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any trouble.  
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I drew out an arrow from a young man that had pierced the fat of his eye below the skin, and the arrow was embedded, and one could only reach the point toward the fletching, and the arrow was large, the size of a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; 
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The game was healed, and no evil accident came to it. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: 
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beard, and I worked delicately until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.  
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew an arrow from a man, which had fallen in his belly, and I thought he would die; 
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and I dug around it, and drew it out forcefully, and he did not have any bad accident. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man to whom an arrow had fallen in the back, and the wound was sealed over it;  
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural state, nor did he find harm in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sewn. 
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he remained thus without suffering great pain; 
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And treat an arrow for a prince's man, the king, which had fallen between his nose and cheek, and was leaning slightly to the right side. 
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it after it had fallen for three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I carefully removed it all at once, and he did not feel it at all.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt numbness and pain under his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I put a plaster on the spot that was atractive and digestible so that the tissues would not swell. 
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the points of the arrow appeared to me. 
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied a plaster for several days and sewed up the wound deeply, and kept the patient still for a long time until he felt the arrow one day within his flesh. 
et il le me dist.	And he told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put a strongly caustic medicine on the wound for several days until it was open and I probed it and felt the head of the arrow moving in its place. 
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I widened the opening of the wound with that caustic medicine until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me. 
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And I carefully passed the time for four months, and then widened the wound so that I could insert the forceps and pull it from one side and the other, but it would not come out.  
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then do not cease to refine and engineer ways of instruments, until I took it one day as well-made forceps, according to the form which will come at the end of this chapter, until I tried them, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And many judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: 
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was healed entirely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your practice on what I do not say, for books cannot grasp everything; 
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters compare on very few things, and on what is present and lacking, find nine works, and nine instruments, at the dismantling of strange things which happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs where they are stuck except according to two manners: 
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either by the place where they enter, or by another part; 
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that comes out by the place where it enters is an arrow that enters the flesh, and rarely comes out now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh is rotted around it, and the passage is opened. 
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it every day.  
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it will come out; and if it does not, pierce around it with a fine awl until the flesh around it is widened, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the skull and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: 
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you do not milk it, but leave it until it is equal after some days, for if the arrow comes up to the bone, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck further than in the bone alone, and does not reach as far as the sinews, and the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then one may extract it with an engine.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very stuck in this way and cannot come out by force, then administer splints around it, as I have told you. 
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place until it is healed. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that one cannot see it, then one must search for all of it. 
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, draw it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then make the wound larger. 
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it is held, remove the flesh that is stuck to it in two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it. 
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And subtly, even though you do not break the arrow, draw it more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the sinews around it are rotten, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then apply what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; 
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting a nerve or vein, and put it in any way you can draw the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently; 
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and position the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow fell upon them, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place them according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	An arrow that has come from another direction, or where there appears to be something of it, or the skin is swollen in a place if one sees or feels it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut above, so that the tongs can grasp it, and then extract it: 
si saut fuer maintenant.	If a leap must be made now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone and widens the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then start the extraction again until it comes out. 
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if there is an arrow in it, push it all the way through.  
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if it is a bone, and you see that pushing is necessary, administer the instrument with its point, so that the point of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument. 
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	Then push it in; and if the arrow is barbed, put the instrument with its point entering inwards, to ease extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is in a bone or muscle or belly or bladder or side, and it is close by, and you can cover it up, then cover it.  
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful not to cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary. 
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the cure as long as it is healthy. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs with which we treat arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways of doing so:  
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the butt end is like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as it is in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the forceps for pushing and pulling is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are XXXI veins from which one heals oneself, of which it has or head XVI, that is to know: 
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two pulsating ones which are after the ears, which are called the two "herbages";  
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	And the two arteries which are in the two apparent temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspirers"; 
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein which is on the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the head above the nose; 
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two cords which are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins which are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and you see those that are under the tongue 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly healed are five in each arm:  
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and common people call it "vein of the head"; 
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and common people call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossa, and it is the one which is healed, which appears manifestly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvation is the vein which is between the auricular and the annular, and it has two branches; 
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: 
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	The first one is below the curvature of the pocket of the left side, and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the right side. 
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the vein that is called "nesse," which is in the ankle of the other side; 
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins below those ones. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein of the head which is behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of the vein, as I tell you, are that you raise up the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a coarse cloth. 
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then twist the patient's neck with a vise until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Where your thumbs are, and where you feel the pulse beneath your thumb, there is a sign of an artery. 
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet and put it under the vein until the bone, then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards, and cut and loosen the skin and the vein well. Two should go through, and make blood come out as much as you see. 
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then bind and tie it until it is healed. 
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The lancing of the two arteries which are in the two temples is good for ancient migraines and habitual ophthalmia and for the flow of sharp tears as well. 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the lancing is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens their neck until the two veins appear openly.  
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And put your thumb under your index finger and then cut a small amount. 
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the skin above the vein at its highest point with your index finger and insert the lancet below, lift the vein upwards, and tie it off just as you have done for the other two veins; let run enough blood according to your need. 
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then untie the patient and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.  
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then bandage it firmly and leave it until it is healed. 
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have already spoken of their tying off and extraction, which is the beginning of this book.  
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	Bleeding from the vein in the forehead is worth as much as bleeding from the cephalic vein for old facial ailments, migraine, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient twists their neck until the vein appears. 
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is this: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and hold it steady with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see. 
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then untie the patient's collar, and tie the vein tightly until it is healthy and no longer bleeds or oozes. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it must not be too severe.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And the cutting should not be across the bone because the bone is close and may break the vein if it is thin.  
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	Cutting the two veins that are in the two temples helps with headaches, and swelling, and redness, and pain in the eye, and diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their cutting is such that the patient tightens his collar by twisting a bandage as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the healthy one, and let it be a sinue, a long poke with a flame a wide poke, for there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break; 
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make the blood run, as much as you need, and then tie it on cotton, and tie it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The sinue of the vein of the nose is good for fever and for strong headache, and for diseases of the face such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of the sinue is that the patient pinches his neck, then strains his nose with your left hand, and takes a long subtle flame, and puts it in between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not apply too much pressure, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bandage it for a night, because it is quickly restored. 
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The juice of two guindeges helps with the constriction of the veins, and at the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and esthiomenas; 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the juice is that the patient constricts his neck under one and the other, as we have said; 
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the masters stand above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a stool, then they lance the vein for a long time widely, then draw blood temperately, or as much as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then redo it in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and loosen all the veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle. 
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And leave it until morning so that the wound may heal. 
de la sainie des leivres	From the vein of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sinews of the veins above the lips help to glue in the mouth, and cause corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and pain and inflammation.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is to have the patient sit in front of you and pull out his collar as I have said. 
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn back the lip and look at the two veins, one is at the right lip and the other at the left, and you recognize them because they are black, and because around them are small black veins. 
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Cut both, and if you don't recognize them and are in doubt, cut the largest one on each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of the veins below the tongue is done after the healing of the cephalic vein and this is for the tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the healer is such that the patient sits between his hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein. 
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Heal then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the knife with which one commonly heals are healed according to two manners: 
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by puncturing all with a sharp pointed blade, or with an olive-wood subtle tool like cutting knives, and it is called “anesil”; 
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are broad and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the burning iron is very famous, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And one must open the raised veins full of apparent thick blood, and that contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive-wood blade:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle pointed, and it is for cutting the subtle veins where there is subtle citric blood
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps ailments that are below the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly; 
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it behooves the healer that he bleed it abundantly, and that he guard against the artery which is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it behooves him to staunch it, as I have said; 
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And it should not be piercing the flame, but cutting like a knife.  
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it behooves you to extract it, and change another; 
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want any vein of it, or you bleed in place of it the vein below the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens manifestly; 
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And apply the cautery to the flame, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location of the vein, it is necessary that you extract the arm, and touch the area until you feel the pulse. 
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the location for the incision, then bind the arm, and apply the cautery to the vein with a flame.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And be careful not to wound the artery when you see the swollen area, for it is an artery: 
eschui la donques.	Avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protrude upwards like the urine of a child, and its color is red and delicate, know that it is the sinew of an artery: 
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and place your finger along its length, then remove your finger if the sinew shrinks back, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Bind the arm, and leave it so, and do not move it the patient; 
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not stopped, and it comes to you, and the medicine is not present to you, then bind the artery if it is open, for the head of the retractor.  
et estainche li sans.	And stop the blood. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark of fig, and split it, and take one of the halves and bind it on well until the next day. 
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the blood is stopped, it is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, if the healer, as we have said, uses powders that stop blood;  
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping is not greasy in several positions because of the small size of the wound, and the strength of the bandage on the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein of the arm in the middle helps it draw blood from above the head and below the body because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said. 
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it is necessary for the phlebotomist to be careful of the nerve that is below, and if he cuts too deeply and finds the nerve, it will swell and the wound will become sore and perhaps cannot heal. 
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some people because of its subtlety, then you must lance the instrument numb. 
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And avoid the nerve as best you can. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein of the cephalic helps it draw blood from the head and helps with those things.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to cut in the middle with olive oil or myrtle oil flame because it is the safest of all veins, for it has no nerve nor artery below. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and do not be bothered if one must start over the first time. 
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance some men's veins swell at the first attempt, but it does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the cautery is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing that you must know about healing is that healing is administered only to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses; 
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the healing be done in one of the three ways which are here stated:  
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic; 
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of spring in youth, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; 
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours from the start of the day.  
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The saint which is administered to sick people has no determined hour, but only when need is by day or night, in all hours and at all times.  
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it does not suit to administer the sacrament to children until 14 years, nor to a woman carrying [a child] before the fourth month until the seventh.  
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They ought not to be bled those who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wants to be administered the sacrament, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that he purify his bowels with a light clyster, if he has much retained phlegm, so that the veins do not draw from the bowels harmful superfluities dangerous to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor should one who is too full of meat, nor who is drunk so that he is filled with wine, nor those with dropsy be administered the sacrament.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And one should refrain from administering the sacrament after a colic attack, vomiting, discharge of the bowels, and multiplication of birth pains in women, and labor, staying awake, and fasting, and to those whose virtue has entirely departed, or through something of the arms or body. 
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtly reduce the humors, if it is large without, through food and drink and through medicine, if you have the power.  
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter a bath, if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed from a vein between the wrist and elbow, as we have said. 
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard yourself that day from work, and from pain, and from lust, and from similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be bound and joyful, and let the bandages be higher than those on whom you bleed, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the bandage moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot stop the blood.  
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and you can feel them. 
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the bandages with a drop of old oil, then put your index finger of your left hand on that vein below the place where you want to bleed so that the vein does not move and fail when cut. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee as cords in a snare, and if some are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these. 
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason it is necessary that the bleeders be advised in these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good. 
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, one begins again a bit lower than that place or higher hastily, if the veins are not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the veins are swollen and the patient is frightened, one leaves him for a day or two, and does not tie the arm. 
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps abscesses will come.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter a bath, then begin the bleeding again if it pleases him. 
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the puncture is small, or the blood runs subtly and you doubt that it will not issue as much blood as you see, then put the flame directly into that puncture itself. 
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And perform the work quickly so that the veins become swollen. 
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this often happens when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the bleeding again, and put a poultice of oil on it. For it alleviates the body of blood, and the oil softens in that place where the oil is placed. 
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the poultice of oil in every bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stanch the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and the same thing makes a triangle and a bulge of it, when it is put back in place. 
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if subtle the sinew tears apart when it is too thick.  
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess comes, which happens often, even when it is not drained except at this time when the opening of the vein is small, if you hurry, and put on the place a sponge moistened in hot water and salt for one hour. 
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it must be done after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it stays in place after a few days without any blackness or greenish color, then do not harm it. 
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see it, put on some aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mustard, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there appears an abscess and swelling at the site of the vein-opening: 
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put your hand on it then, and if you find the place soft when pressing with your hand, that appearance is bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore, do not put on anything of what we have said, for fear of cutting an artery. 
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But make a dry plaster to harden the area, then treat it with another dressing until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red.  
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see it thick, let it flow out until it is thin. 
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down.  
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, make a larger wound, and let the incision be wide. 
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it should be bled a little and often, and one must bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking.  
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of incision is safe from bleeding and severing of nerves, and it is worth more than the incision that is long or wide. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to him whose body lacks strength for the incision, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; 
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is heated, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, give him softened bread in thick syrup or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chick peas, and a well-smelling syrup.  
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after the flow of much blood, it is fitting that he inhale broth of flesh and fragrant subtle syrup and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to avoid weakening his arm and bleeding another time, it is fitting that when he is weakened by a great bloodletting, he should bleed a little at a time, according to the amount of his strength continuing.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to sever his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong flesh, should bleed for seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another place, it must be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has much blood within his body which is already heated, and it brings fever; 
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so it is fitting to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening so that he sweats abundantly.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	After you have observed all the conditions of incision, and place your hand on his pulse as he is incised, so that death does not come in place of sweating, and this happens many times when the surgeon is negligent.  
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not right when you see to detach the arm, and make blood come out the second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly upon it. 
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	And if it is crooked, that he extend the arm quickly, for that would be bad; 
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	But let it stay until it heals the second time; 
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Or you place the tip of the flame there, as long as the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein comes out strong, and put a piece of silk sharpened to a point on it, and press lightly upon it. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, if the blood in that place itself, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein above the arm is cut in place of the head vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the healing is that the patient plunges their hand into hot water, as long as the wrist turns red; 
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it is tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, then heal it now crosswise, not lengthwise nor wide; 
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the opening be wide, and cut very close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood run into the hot water until you have enough. 
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is summer, do not put the hand in hot water at all, for one puts it more in winter than in summer. 
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the cutting of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	Cutting the vein on the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand tight, and put it in hot water until the vein swells up so that you can see it. 
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if you cut across it, and even if you sever it completely, it doesn't matter.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not press too hard, for the nerves are underneath all exposed flesh, and then put the hand in hot water, if it is frozen in the wound and cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as needed, put oil and salt on the vein to heal quickly, and do so for every vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sinew of the hand on the left is equal to the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have told you on the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The herb of the sophene is worth against all illnesses that are below the body, such as illness of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and illness of the reins, and of the thighs and legs that are old, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its sinew is such that the patient plunges his foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it bursts, and ties above the joint of the foot. 
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And the vein is at the ankle, and many rains go from above the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So choose then a larger vein or one at the ankle that moves well. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you sinew it on the foot, be careful of the nerves underneath, and sinew across as if cutting.  
et soit li flaimes anesil.	And let the flame be gentle. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back into hot water, and let the vein be well emptied.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the sinewing fails the first time, start again a little further up, for the flesh is salty.  
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do the same to the sinew of the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of strong men, and its blood is worth the pain of the hip when it's for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his sinew is such that the patient enters or bathes, and strains upon the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein. 
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, strain the sinew in all the ways that you can, and by crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it off, for the flesh is underneath, and it is very strong in men's hands. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, strain any sinew of his that opens or runs down both feet and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And draw as much blood as you see, then untie the ligature, and put cotton on top and remove it; 
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	from cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping vessels are made of horn, or of ivy, or glass. 
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And cupping is done in two ways:  
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping which is done without cutting is also done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with heat, or without heat. 
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And cupping which is done by cutting and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is entirely on the head. 
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are along the neck. 
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on the sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping vessel below the chin. 
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping vessels on the two shoulders. 
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glass upon the boils; 
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping glasses applied to both arms; 
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping glasses on both legs;  
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping glasses on both ankles; 
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not draw blood, except for a few small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken anyone, as one does when bleeding from a vein; 
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not fitting that it be administered, neither with full heat nor without heat, in any illness which comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illnesses it is fitting to cup, or for customs, then we administer them every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and both in between. 
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; 
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if some find fullness and redness in their face, and head, and neck, and darkness as well. 
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood;  
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are some who faint, and see by night blood and sadness and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is the least humid month, we order them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sinew of the thigh helps with the heaviness of the head ... which comes to it, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; 
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this cupping is in place of the sinew of the cephalic vein, and it is not fitting that those of cold complexion use it, or who have diarrhea, for this does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not suitable for old people to use it, nor those who have cold diseases. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover often become stiff, and therefore it is necessary to put the cupping glass a little lower because of the fear of stiffness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Bloodletting on the neck is in place of the vein and the basilisk, and therefore it is good for constriction of the breast, and for a fissure of the channel of the buttock, and for all, and for fullness. 
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is not advisable to press too hard, because if it holds too firmly, it can cause obstruction or stomach and heart issues. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Bloodletting on the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the vein of the basilisk. 
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is necessary that you instruct the patient to press their hand on the spot, so they do not cut an artery, and there is no flowing of blood. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The applications of cupping below the chin are good for diseases of the mouth, and for the rotting of gums, and similar illnesses which are in the mouth.  
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in place of the health of the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Cupping on the arms is as effective as three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins. 
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the patient not to make too strong a suction, for the flesh is naked of fat, and under it are nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	A cup placed on the buttock is good for hemorrhoids in the fundament, and for illnesses below it, and it should be large, and made of iron so that it draws well. 
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And by chance, if it were delicate, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and it would make large wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	If the cupping glasses on the legs bleed freely, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the kidneys, and bladder, and loosen tumors; 
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And they are placed on the two thighs, and the two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause emaciation in many constitutions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply a cupping glass is that you first put it empty, and suck temporarily, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing so, until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redness of the blood; 
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then remove, and replace the cupping glasses, and take care in the constitution of bodies, for there are some who have tough flesh, and clear pores:  
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is fitting to strike only once, and it is fitting to make wide wounds, and a deep prick; 
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is fitting to strike it twice: 
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to thin the way for the thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is fitting to strike it a third time; 
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only strike once.  
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we often restart; 
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, strike deeply and strongly, so that the heart is pierced only slightly, and it is fitting for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have obstructed pores, that you moisten the edges of the cups with oil that is stimulating and dissolving:
