se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; 
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the evening, of cress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or other similar thing. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and suchlike.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if he who is treated has tender flesh and large pores, it is not right to put any oil on it, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or nightshade water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or other similar [water].
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, should get up with watercress, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities, they rise from old wine, or vinegar of honey, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things. 
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not suitable to apply a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two. 
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he wash himself when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are being treated if they are choleric, and if their wound is too painful and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that they take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in season, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little, and roasted meat, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and moderately spiced wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat little birds and pigeons. 
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he will bleed himself, he should drink more than eat. 
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is fitting to give some men three times a nutmeg before the bleeding or after, to comfort the main limbs.  
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the wine be subtle, but it is not right that those who are hot drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	Cupping glasses that are placed without pricking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the thigh, and gout, and on the belly and buttocks and the reins and the hip, because these limbs do not suffer from being pierced, and we only do it to draw blood from limb to limb, just as we put them on the breasts when a baby bleeds;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the viscosity which is at the member, as we put cupping glasses on the belly and on the arm to reduce the member; 
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And remove the pain, when there is swelling or stone, if it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the swelling, or dislodges the stone from its place; 
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And thus it is done when it is put on the liver and on the thigh when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; 
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in illnesses of the pleura, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with hot water in which herbs suitable for this have been cooked. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two hands and a half palm in circumference, and it has around the middle one small hole, as for putting in a needle, and it is made of horn, smooth in front so that it does not injure the patient when putting it on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and he should put in the middle a stick of wood or iron, to place a bandage which holds, and they are big and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; 
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses for children are different from those for old people, and for thin people than for fat people.  
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must put this cupping glass thus on the limb: 
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the bandage of wax or linen, and put it through the cupping glass across the stick which is in the cupping glass, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient;  
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and your hands should be on the hole that we have said, so that when you want, if the vapor goes, you take off the cupping glass; 
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and you take the linen as before, and often start again, if you need to. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass which is administered for sickness of pleurisy, at all times acute, there is neither stalk nor hole, and it is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed upon the limb only. 
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Cupping glasses are not administered except on limbs where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places. 
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in those devoid of flesh, such as bone or sinew, and others similar.  
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of the user is that when you find cupping glasses which are in sweet water clear without stain, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them for one night in sweet water, until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies.  
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then it should be bled by vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put poultices on top. 
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and have shrunk, if it is a place where one can put a cupping glass, then put one on, for this is very helpful afterwards. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place up gently, and then sharply, very well, and then breathe on it. 
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the poultices heal too quickly after the body of the poultice, wet a linen cloth in cold water and put it on top until the poultice is softened. 
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the poultices are multiplied, put crushed vitriol or alum and similar things on top until they are softened.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you can put half a handful of peeled beans on the spot and leave them until they burn at the spot, which will now stop it.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other bandages. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the bandages do not want to stick, rub the area with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until the bandage sticks in it, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will stick. 
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are falling off, sprinkle a pinch of powdered aloe and salt, or ash on top, so they will hold now.  
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, thread of wool, that the fools who speak against this chapter have never seen any of the old books, nor read a letter from them. 
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason is the knowledge estranged in our land, for I never found any good one. 
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I do not know anything else, except through the knowledge of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated this knowledge through experience and through the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained therein and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two previous chapters. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is fitting then that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where wise men put their understanding, and linger on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is fitting that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age. 
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold meats, that is to say, cold stews, and broth of birds and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no fear of a hot abscess, or spreading of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to his first treatment which he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is fitting that one nourishes the patient with meats that produce great nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, and turnips, and veal pie, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at half ignorance it takes more time, and sooner the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot be well set or rejoined according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, such as the bones of young children. 
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But have no care, set the broken bone with large splints that hold it firm and join the limb together, until it is strengthened as it was before. 
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not hasten his work, and for this reason he must be nourished with large meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a head fracture is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone marrow, and another in sharpening, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small crack throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every manner he should have his engine, and his proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to its place. 
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that the bone is broken by the fact that the limb is twisted, and clearly shows by a gap, and sounds when pressed. 
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no crookedness nor sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; 
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but there may well be crookedness, or a crack, or a small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not right to move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that will come after, and then extract it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture which goes in depth, and the two parts are separated, it is necessary to now put them back together equally, just as abscesses come to life; 
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if a hot abscess comes, let it rest for some days until the abscess is soothed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it straight as you can lightly and carefully, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those where there are pieces; 
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then remove it, as it should be done afterwards.  
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into two pieces, whether it is the hand or foot, or at your hand it is a small limb, or at two tendons, or at one tendon and at your hand; 
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are loosened, you should reset all the additions to their places as much as you can, and make sure that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient. 
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust the two ends of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: 
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it sets well and do not force it too much or squeeze it as those who cause boils and contractions in the limb by their work, as we have often seen.  
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while watching nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other way;  
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and make sure that the limb is so secure that he does not feel any pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, except perhaps a little, it is necessary to put him in a position where he feels no pain. 
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And be careful that he is kept straight so that crookedness does not come when it is restored. 
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones: 
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; 
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and strong bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb and hold it equally on all sides so that there is no blemish. 
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie it with light tow bandages, three or four turns according to the limb, and hold your hand firmly on the whole bandage, then go above the break and tighten it less so that the break is then a bit further from the break. 
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy place, then take the other ligament, and return it around directly onto the broken place. 
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then bind the part below the fracture, and remove it moderately, not too hard nor too softly, as we have said in the first chapter above. 
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the bandages strips of linen or cloths, so that they are all equal, then bind everything above with bandages, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing on the hot abscess and that removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days. 
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then remove your splints, and let them be half the width of a walking stick or wood from which they make stakes, or palm reeds, and let them be according to this shape.  
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the plaster which one puts on the break be a bit bigger and wider than the others; 
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should also be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether small or large; 
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then remove the plasters as you did in the first hour, then tie a thread over it neatly, just as in the first hour on the break; 
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	tighter on one side, looser on the other;  
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be medium sized, not too thick nor too thin, and be made of soft linen; 
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in some works of fools who make their bandages from twisted linen threads, that is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not right for there to be less than two fingers' space between each plaster.  
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bruised by the heads of the needles after the tightening in their flesh, then put under them wads of linen, or wool fleece, so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the heart is broken, I will say the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to set all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to put strong splints on before five or seven days, or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess arising; 
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: 
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And it is that you take flour which sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it; this is the common way to make a plaster that restores fractures in many positions, for both women and young children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.  
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way to make a plaster that restores fractures, dislocations, and torsions: 
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take three bay leaves and frankincense and elecampane and asafetida and gum arabic and mastic, each ten drams. 
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Myrrh and aloe, each three drams. 
alechil VIIII З.;	Alcohol nine drams. 
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make them into powder and mix them with the white of an egg.  
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the man's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly restores broken bones and is worth much to many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another kind of plaster that is worth using for twisting:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and woundwort, each ten drams. 
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Myrrh and aloe, each nine drams.  
acaice VI З.;	Acacia six drams.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Armenian bole ten drams, and grind well, and cook with rose water or the white of an egg and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another kind of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and eases the pain arising from it, and heals the use of the bone, and breaks it:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new linen cloth, and moisten it in oil and honey, and place it on the area. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for calming a hot abscess and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to make a plaster that restores broken bones: 
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of plaster for restoring a broken bone and for drawing out the matter from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take mallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, of each one part; 
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind them, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of plastering stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take mallow roots, flaxseed, betony, melilot, and sanicle, and violet flowers and chamomile flowers, of all one part;  
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind them, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.  
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one should put on the broken limb, to restore it, dry things a little hot, such as myrrh and aloes and frankincense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another manner of plaster that is good for injury and pain: 
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take marjoram and goat hairs cut off, or bird feathers, and vipers bugloss, and cut them equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and bind it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then unbind it a little while after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that the bone has moved from its place; 
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not, unbind it in a few days.  
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, feeling of rest or swelling, then hurry, unbind it and remove the plaster now;  
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light linen cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and plunge it in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is relieved;  
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen cloth on it moistened with water or rose oil, and bind a bandage over it, until you are sure of a warm abscess; 
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and lay the inflammation of the limb to rest, and let the pain be removed, then resume the binding subtly, and a piece of plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before; 
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and subtly until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess has pus and is red, painful, and swollen, when all of it has been removed, and you need plaster and bandages, do so again as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, do not unbind it except after III days or IV or V or VII; 
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leave it for XX days, according to what is seen, until the fracture heals and brings the adjustment of the flesh close;  
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then the restraint more than the first, and it thickens its flesh, as I have said before; 
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place dry more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there;  
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	so then apply a sharp hot wet compress, every time you unbind it, and do this every third day, and loosen a piece of the bandage; 
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	By this work then cut the nourishing to the limb, and quickly amend what the foolish mind does, that restores the limb crookedly. 
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is bad, and if it are works feared, and I do not see other thing than to leave it alone and work straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many manners of breaks are there, and various figures, and the causes are destined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are breaks that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck bone breaks all the bone up to the sinew which is beneath the bone, as it makes hay or wood.  
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And for this reason this manner of break is called "haichure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword cuts the bone above without piercing it, and this manner of break is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And the wound from these two breaks is large or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fissure, or blows of stone, or falls on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture extending near the membrane that is beneath the bone or above it, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if a wound that is healed in the bone as fine as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture “capillary”; 
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and it makes the piece of bone go down inside, and the edges are shaved as smiths do when they strike on anvils; 
si entre li piere dedens.	If the stone enters within. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have soft or moist bones, such as the skull of a child; 
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are detached from them like chips;  
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the probing with instruments, and by the corrupted flesh which is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similar hair is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs a little upon it, if it appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to the patient's condition, and if you see any bad symptom, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, stretching, trembling, fever, and the eyes coming out and becoming red, and other similar things in various states, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeless accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone becomes corrupted and accidents occur as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the fractured part thus: 
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and take the head of the sick person and uncover it on the bone in all ways that you can, and over the figure of the wound as much as you can, and if discharge of blood comes when uncovering the bone, or abscess comes out, help him with what is necessary and fill the place with cloths softened in rose oil; 
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscess that comes out is appeased and be sure of the discharge of blood; 
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two ways of working: 
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is if you cut a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:  
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he puts another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second way is if you have a number of incisions of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are of unbreakable iron; 
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly so you do not bruise the head 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce it around, so that you administer cuts with rasps, but make sure they do not pierce beyond the bone where you are testing, and it must have above the point a margin or a circle, so that it does not let the point go beyond the bone. 
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And you must have several of them, so that each one comes in its place according to the type of bone, so that you have rasps for all of them. 
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three kinds of rasps: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put the rasp on the bone and turn it at your wrists as much as you know the bone is pierced. 
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the rasp another place a little after, and so do all around, then cut with nippers the space of the bone that is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, as long as you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pincers.  
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and guard that you do not touch the brain nor the sciatic nerve. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, it is fitting that you leave the instrument which remains from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisor. 
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if any of the small bones or scales remain, lightly remove them with instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of working is that which Galien says, which is safer.  
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and praise him very highly, for this is his word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place below the head of this lenticular incisor, of which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharp on two sides so that the cutting edge is towards the bone.  
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike with a small mallet above so that you gently tap the bone all around and be careful of the cloth beneath. 
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is near the bone, strike lightly for you can strike it well without harm and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce as far as the fabric, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then you must scrape away that roughness and remove the scales with a delicate razor, which you should have in various quantities to administer in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you shave before using large razors, and then after with more subtle ones, and do not cease to do so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other delicate clippings and fractures, it is fitting that you administer care according to its direction.  
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that is not answered by one who has put his study into this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the fracture is exposed, it is fitting that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it upon the wound; 
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it upon the first cloth. 
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as lightly as you can so that you don't burden the wound, then apply another bandage over it, and don't tighten it any more than is necessary to hold the wound together; 
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess has quieted down, then untie it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, frankincense powder, birthwort, and similar things; 
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make a powder out of these things, and put it on the wound, and then apply cleansing medicines without biting. 
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and make sure that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, and do not allow pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the cloth covering the brain, it will run and spread, and cause the patient great harm;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts upon the cheek a biting thing it stings above 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come except from the medicine that one has put upon it, because of its virtue, it is fitting that you take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and make a paste with them. 
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it in ways that are fitting until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for there are two bones. 
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that below is cartilaginous and does not break; it only makes a bend or twist, and then heals.  
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is fitting that you bite your little finger or thumb above the nose, and put the broken part inside against your index finger, and with a pouch by pressing, until the nose returns according to its natural shape. 
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part above the knee, and the bone cannot return to its place, it must be set even with the top of a large nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, do it again in the same way and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can. 
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling of the abscess has subsided, then bind the fractured part with two strips of linen cloths, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	You bind one on the other side, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the strips be so wide that they fill the spaces of the bone. 
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer should moisten the bandages with butter, and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they be softened in a preparation of egg yolk and mill powder;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the bandage on until the bone is solid and the cartilage is hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes put goose quills instead of bandages, and if the wound is covered with linen, hold it still, and let the patient blow on it.  
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or do what you see. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if boils come to a head while you are working on them, put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a poppy seed decoction.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not come out, apply a plaster on top made of sesame flour and frankincense powder mixed with egg yolk, then put it on light bandages and do not tie them.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the broken bone is small and it is broken into many pieces, remove it with suitable instruments, then sew up the wound and treat it with things that promote healing of flesh and bone, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this. 
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the bone, treat it with bandages and put splints of plank until it heals. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated downward and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only superficial and not broken in two, but rather pushed inward, so the expert can easily recognize it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; 
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is in the left mandible, put your index finger of your right hand in it and gently push the fracture inward and hold it with the other hand by force and make it equal. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is broken in two, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, so that it may be equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth move or are broken, tie them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then apply cerate to the fractured jaw and put a double cloth on top; 
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put a large well-made splint on top of the cloth, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up at the points you can reach, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, loosen it on the third day and then reset what has changed; 
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put plaster on it, made from powdered mill flour with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the cerote. 
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put a light linen cloth over the plaster; and if the plaster dries out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed. 
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess arises, do as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, consider whether any piece of bone has been removed;  
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if it is subtle, use suitable instruments for this. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, if the wound is large, sew it up, and put suitable plasters on it, to encourage flesh to grow, until it is healed.
de la forcele	Of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The clavicle breaks several times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: 
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	either it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and this is the easiest to restore;  
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Where there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the works are such that when the fracture is without a wound, you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the broken bone is; 
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the side;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put the fracture at your feet so that the form is as it should be and there is neither appearance nor protrusion. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, put under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and let it be large according to your necessity; 
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and lift the broken bone, and pull out the sphere with your hand so that you set the fracture as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the humerus back out because it comes in perfectly, then it is fitting that the patient lie often on his shoulder blade, and put under the shoulder a medium pillow, and have assistants push the shoulder down, until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then straighten the fracture at your feet, and if you find it broken, it is necessary to cut it open;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and treat the fragments lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any pressure, then apply it to one of the incisors that you have. 
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put this instrument under the forceps, to hold the joint: 
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not sharpened, and should be as wide as the bone requires, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; 
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two heads, as you see, and one is wide, and the other narrow, according to the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; 
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of the hot cautery, if the wound burns and the rupture is small or you doubt the hot cautery, then apply the wound with cloths and bandages according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if boils come, moisten a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The constriction of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone a plaster of powder from the mill and yolk of egg, and put light bandages on top, and put a splint underneath the armpit if you need it. 
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage of a palm's width, and put a double layer of linen on top of the bandages and plaster. 
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a subtle splint of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And put the splint on top of the fracture, and turn the bandage up over the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sick armpit.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And loosen from each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture properly, and you see clearly that the splint does not move on top of the broken bone, then leave it alone each day, and when the ligaments become slack, then tighten it. 
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps put a small pillow under his armpit to lift the shoulder up; 
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if it lightens the fracture of the collarbone by lifting the shoulder, then tie his arm to his neck and do not untie it until twenty days have passed lest a bad accident occurs; 
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then begin the plaster again, if you see he needs it, and remove it and leave him like that until he is restored. 
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and less for some men.  
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It sometimes happens that the broken shoulder or the wide place does not heal in the middle, and it should not be forced except by touch; 
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if you arrange it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form in all the ways that you can; 
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put on the place powder from the mill with plenty of egg white, and light bandages, and put on a double cloth; 
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on a wide and subtle splint, a bit larger than the shoulder, and under the splint are shavings in no place of the shoulder, so use those shavings of linen bandages so that the splint lies evenly; 
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then bind it all with a large bandage firmly so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the binding each day; 
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it loosens, if you bind it and put the splint equal if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on their side; 
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in XX days or in XXV. 
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is fulfilled, untie it, and be sure, for it is not bone that is put out lightly. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out in front and not below the heart, then make a poultice, and have the surgeon do what we have said for the fracture of the collarbone to soothe the abscess with heat.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is sometimes broken in half, but this rarely happens; 
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it falls below, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and all at once, and by chance vomits blood, and the hair appears in the broken bone, and one can feel it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back and puts a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and assembles the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and subtly make them equal in all ways as you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; 
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put plasters and bandages on the broken bone with a fine powder of salt or another light substance, and wrap it in a cloth, tying it above the broken bone so that it does not move; 
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage around the back, and loosen it gradually, and check every hour if the bandage is loosening, and if it loosens, tighten it. 
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to untie it because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and remove the plaster, and treat what has come in a manner of cures. 
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then loosen the plaster, and remove it until it is healed. 
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of ribs only comes from their great size after the back, and chiefly within, and they only break because they are slippery; 
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one can well tell by inquiry what it is.  
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a plaster, and remove it with a spatula, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of ribs leans inward, then the patient feels great pain and sharp points, as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the tissue. 
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and has pains and coughs up a great deal of blood, and it is a very serious ailment and the ancients have considered it a great danger.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is fitting to administer meats that inflate the belly, to expel the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, so that hot abscesses will not come, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, so be healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And say none of you where we put cupping glasses on the spot, to suck out pus, and it seems reasonable. 
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw the superfluities to the spot due to weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the place with linen soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the binding even around, then it is cured by the cure of pleurisy, of meat and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure due to the bone pointing through the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the spot of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put something under the instrument to protect the flesh. 
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one should cut the bone and pull it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and dress it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses come, put soft cloths soaked in rose oil on the spot. 
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it while the place of this which it is necessary for an abscess, and let it lie often on the side where it should be, as long as it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bone near the neck, and sometimes it happens that it rains;  
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also at the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know whether they will be healed or not, if you notice their hands are softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in several positions, and if he moves them and feels well when they are removed and pressed, know that the juncture of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if care is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know whether it will heal or not, see if its limbs are softened, and if the accidents which are in its hands are soft, and on the back there is flatulence and discharge without will; 
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has turned it on its belly, there is discharge without will.  
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and he wants to rise up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal: 
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if one does not labor in its treatment. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you warm it if there is a hot abscess, and put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed; 
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; 
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.  
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bones are broken, it is necessary to cover them on a hearth; 
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with stitches, then cure it with ointment containing charcoal, until it is healed;  
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," put your left hand in your pocket and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then put the plaster and splint on top, if you need them; 
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then remove it, and if there are broken bones, set them up and the bone setter heals the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It sometimes happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does happen, there would only be a slight decrease in height. 
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And bend down long, and incline toward the side, and comes to the patient pain in the place, and throbbing, and swelling as it breaks.  
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above, as far as you are above the fracture; 
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what the fracture is and its shape. 
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the fracture is only at the head, you set that fracture equal as long as it is in its natural shape.
