Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it slopes inward, make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture appears to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it equal, put a plaster on it, then put a splint of wood or horn on top, and hold the fracture so that it does not move.  
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And apply the place beneath the ribs, as long as the ligature is equal. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a hot abscess comes, do not touch it until the hot abscess is calmed down, and put on what we have said before. 
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	And then return to restoration, and extract it as it should be done, if there is no bad accident; 
et c’est li maniere.	And that is the manner. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of two manners: 
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	One of which is that you take a smooth stick of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two ends with two ties, and lift them up high, and have the patient sit on the seat. 
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then take the broken arm and bind it on a stick, so that it reaches the armpit, and put a curve in the stick. Then hang it on something heavy or have someone hold it down. 
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place your hands together at the point of the break, so that the break returns as it should.  
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one lays the patient on his back and ties his hand to his neck; then he commands two assistants, that one hold what is on the fracture with his hands, and the other hold below all of the ligament, and each stretches in their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is close to the head of the shoulder, you should put one bandage below the armpit and the other toward the elbow, below the break.  
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And if the break is toward the elbow, it is best to put a bandage lightly and without strain, so that the break is aligned on the arm and at the elbow. 
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then align the break as it should be and bind it, unless abscesses appear.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess arises, do not extract it until seven days have passed, and place moist linen soaked in rose oil on it until the abscess has subsided; 
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then extract it, and the way to extract it is that you put a plaster on the break, then assemble the arm on the shoulder joint, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest. 
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And put the cloth on it, and extract it on the shoulder joint, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone has not been moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone has moved, then use splints and put on the break a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have two finger-widths of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends three finger-widths beyond the break on each side; 
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then pull upward on the splinters, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter about fractures, harder and less in distance. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the splinters and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you are restoring the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess heat, let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said. 
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look at the bandage every three days, so that it does not itch or swell, or come to the place where the nourishments cannot come to the limb because it is too tight. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the shoulder, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if none of these accidents come, then do not unbind it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach. 
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	And put under the shoulder one cushion plain of wool equally, and look every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandages are loosened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it is treated by the power of medicine, and you give it the meat that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; 
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, let it be thick. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be recovered in forty days altogether; 
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then you must loosen it and administer baths and ointments for healing to straighten the place. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and tight, it will remain for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus," one of which is small, and it is the one that enters the pouch; 
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, toward the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	sometimes only the large humerus breaks, or sometimes the small one, and sometimes both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When small bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; 
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when large ones are broken, so is the healing difficult, and more grievous than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is a small bone that is broken alone, then you must gently stretch it, and set it equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a large bone, it is necessary to bind it more tightly; 
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed upon himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any hardship; 
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the minister's left arm to the part below his hand, or at the ligament, and another minister above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one back in its place, and if there is any detached that the heart grasps, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a splint and set the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a particular chapter; 
si pren la cure.	if you take the care 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of restoration boils arise, then apply a poultice made of rose oil and white wax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; 
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie the poultice on subtly, until the boils are appeased. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	Then remove the wax, and apply a plaster of mill powder with plenty of egg yolk, then apply splints, and let the splint from the fracture be stronger now, and a little wider than the others; 
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have six splints or arms in several positions:  
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and place it higher above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	And let the bandages that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; 
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And let the thread with which it is bound be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is fitting that you bathe the limb in hot water, until the itching is appeased;  
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be tightly bound when at rest. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone loosened, and similar things, so address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you fear that the nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it like that for several days until the nourishment arrives, and then remove it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, then do not loosen it for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	If he is in pain, then let him hold his hands at his neck and let his collars be even, and beware of movement and exertion, and sleep on his back;  
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the humors and constitutions of the patient. 
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at our fingers there are many small breaks, and they only come with weeping often.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is fitting that the patient sits upright and straight in front of him equally; 
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then place his hand on the extended table and extend the broken bones and set them equal to the others, so that they are well joined. 
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And apply a plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not appear, then he applies a splint according to the quantity of the place. 
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And it should be wrapped in a linen cloth. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the base near the belly of the palm, make a sphere of cloths and instruct the patient to squeeze it to his broken palm.  
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as is fitting.  
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the wrist, it is necessary that you put a splint above and another below on the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and bind the two splints together.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if a fracture occurs to any of our two arms, it is the elbow, then set it straight, as it should be. 
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And pull it out with the palm of your hand, and if you see that it will raise a small straight stick to lift the fracture, and it does not move. 
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the fracture is in one of the other arms, like the index finger or one of the others, then set it straight and bind it with the healthy arm that is next to it. 
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	Or you tie them all together, as strong as possible, or put them on a stick, like a pouch.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And take care in the restoration and arrangement of a heated abscess, and heal those who come to you, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns forward and backward. 
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and its restoration is done by tying one linen above the fracture, and the other below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his linen to his own side equally;  
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is near the bone. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, one of the splints should be towards the hip, and the other splints below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the linen be below the knee, and the extension downwards; 
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the splints on the bone equal with his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and the bandage, so that abscesses do not form. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	the binding is done in this manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap it up on the break with a bandage doubled twice in two or three layers, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put one thread long between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the head of the thread above. 
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put on the break splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg. 
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then fill the place eight between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make equal the tightening, then begin to tie three or four turns on the break.  
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And when you go higher above the break, tighten it less. 
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take the two ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints which are above them, then go back down to the head of the thread, as far as you come below the foot. 
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, until neither an abscess nor swelling nor any similar thing comes. 
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it should happen, and it loosens, and corrects what comes as we have said many times; 
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that stick out, it must be drawn out, if one can.  
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, it is necessary to split the place and draw forcefully. 
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And when the thigh is broken like this and splints are put on it as in the shoulder or arm;  
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	in all ways, with restoration done like this, the patient does not weaken.  
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 10 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the furrow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the knee joint there is often no fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, except for a crack or hole, and occurs at any wound, and even without a wound, it is good for everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one puts together what is broken to its proper place as much as it can be assembled. 
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the plaster, and put a round star on it, if you need one, and remove it as is appropriate, then consider all the arrangements that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as a hot abscess and other similar things. 
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Apply to each ailment what is appropriate for it, until it is healed. 
de la brisure de la jambe	From the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called "mustelz," and the other is called "foscile." 
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And every other fracture occurs as it does in the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is all one. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, turn them back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain felt, and it is clearly seen.
et torne desoz.	and turn below. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply extension, and put it equal, and bind the splints equally; 
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, the extension should be less and lighter; 
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and adjust according to your skill. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two bandages of beech wood that can bind the leg on one side and the other, and they should be as long as the leg from the knee down; 
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap them twice above and below, and tie them in the middle as well, and with this bandage, the leg cannot lean to the right or left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should apply splints as long as the leg, and if they are made of wood, they should be placed on the leg to prevent movement, and properly done, this is done in the fracture or where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And stir each day the leg to see if there is a hot abscess or another incident. 
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the cure lasts as long as it is healthy. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and are crushed, and there is strength only in several positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens that a bone of the foot is broken, and you see these bones rise against each other, put the patient's foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, and press it so hard that they return to their place. 
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then put the plaster and bandages on top, and put under the belly of the foot a small table with two sides plain, then straighten the foot carefully, and after you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things which you need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the two are broken, restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand;  
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and let it be one span wider, then place below the foot that table which I have mentioned, and bind it carefully. 
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then place on each bone a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the table below the foot. 
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And let it be placed on the head of the table beneath the belly of the foot so that it holds it well.  
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is fitting that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said. 
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each incident as it is fitting.  
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone where the dagger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, make her sit wide-legged, then incline her to the back, and have her held from behind.  
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the bowl with cotton soaked in the nature of the ailment; and put as much in as I stand. 
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then lift the woman up, and gently tap her back, bit by bit, and then let the cotton jump until it reaches the entrance of the ailment, and return the bone with the hand. 
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days or so. 
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	The fracture will be restored, and if you see it, take a bladder of a lark, tie a cane to the opening, and insert the whole bladder into the ailment.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow into the cane until the bladder is inflated inside. 
la nature si revenra li brisure;	The ailment will return the fracture to its place.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it is healed.  
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of a man's shoulder, or a woman's, is broken, if you restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; 
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice to it, and understand my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture indicates in several ways the right path of restoration: 
enten le donques.	understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	When a penis is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; 
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or more, and it will heal quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	From fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be cleansed now, so that the cleansings that we have said bear witness to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, and there remains vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess comes, leave the restoration until the next day, until the abscess is soothed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause evil accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent upon the heart uncovered, it befits that you put it in place lightly with your hands, with small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension does not appear to you to be equal to your hands, then take this instrument of iron which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary for the healer to employ three or four, according to what they need in each treatment of a fracture. 
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let there be a round one and a large knob, that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it be wide in front, and thick from the middle forward, like this: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called a "palanche," for which reason it is necessary that the curved head be placed on the visible head of the bone; 
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and the end at once, so that it returns, and is equal one against the other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot grasp the bone well, it is necessary that you cut off the head of the bone so that the instruments have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, if there is a point of an instrument suitable for this, either an incision tool or saw, at your disposal; 
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then cut away what remains in the bone from sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do so that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; 
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put any cerate or other thing on the wound where there is oil, lest it cause decay and corruption; 
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and apply a covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; 
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times foolish errors have been made, and they have brought death to the patient or corrupted him sometimes; 
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the binding be looser and softer than for other fractures.  
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not fitting to put on splints; 
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around it, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that pus has formed in the wound, remove what you have put on it and apply a healing ointment, such as tetrafarmacon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is fitting that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is fused and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limb be aligned in such a way that the bone runs down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day it gets worse, and it cannot be soldered but comes back again loose, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must want the wound with a tent, and remove all these detached pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is fitting that you cure it according to what he says in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not draw it out at all, for many times death comes, but leave it until it rots. 
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	Perhaps it will fall off by itself after XX days or XXX, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if you cannot, leave it alone. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From burns that come from solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a sorry sight to see the shape of the limb. 
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	And perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.  
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care, then, if it is fresh to us: 
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if he administers astringent medicines, such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acai, and similar others, so that you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with plenty of egg yolk or with oil; 
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and puts them on the wound in bandages, and binds it well, and does not loosen it for any days. 
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then loosens it, and begins another one, until the nodules are removed. 
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you bind it on a well-made piece of linen;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of linen is that it removes all swellings from the limbs.
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the nodule has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then place a cup on top of it, and make the superfluity appear.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Where you shave it with any razor until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains after the members weak and subtle, it happens for many reasons: 
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	One is because it was bound too tight, and not bound as it should have been;  
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	Or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishments could not come to the limb; 
ou por multitude d’arosement;	Or because of a multitude of movements; 
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	Or for too great movements, not at its proper time;  
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	Or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body tender, so that the blood is multiplied in him; 
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and he administers a bath, and gives him joy and relief; 
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then he puts pitch on the limb, so that the pitch draws out a great inflammation, and he often raises it with hot water, until the inflammation subsides in the limb; 
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and it returns to its natural shape. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a crooked limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: 
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb all over again, and many fools have done this in our land; 
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and it brings great evils, and by chance death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the inflammations and torments are fresh, it is fitting that they be raised with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, roots, melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	And make a softening plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take the juice of mallow and mix it with the fat of a ewe or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top. 
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or you take ripe figs and crush them with flaxseed meal, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation removed by constant and long rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the crookedness is old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with an iron instrument, then it should be cut up to the bone, with a fine, light incision. 
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And put a cushion and care into the treatment. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is necessary now bring it back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if you delay, the wound will swell, and by chance it will be replaced in its place with difficulty.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	Therefore, it is not good to move it at the hour when it is swollen: 
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times bring forth spasm and other pains; 
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	in all ways, when this happens, if you make the patient healthy, then leave him, until his abscess sores are soothed; 
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it lightly, and care for each limb as it comes into its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of the dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It sometimes happens that the jawbones are dislocated both, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	where they are sometimes loosened from their places, and softened a little; 
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are dislocated entirely, and hang towards the ground, and cut off the saliva from his mouth that he cannot hold, nor can close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.  
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through several arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it quickly, and do not delay; 
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the attendants hold the head of the patient, and put their eyes behind the pocket of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; 
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other hand should be unbound, to put it even. 
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he must hold the eye equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if returning it is difficult, even if both jaws are together, apply a mixture of hot water and oil until they soften slightly. 
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not hesitate to return it, as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening it, apply soft cloths with a bandage made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft linens. 
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders should be lying between two cushions so that he doesn't move them neither to the right nor to the left, nor does he make any effort to raise himself, but takes light food as long as the pains are removed, and the jaws are tied; 
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let him eat what he wants lightly, and do not work at opening his mouth to eat or drink as long as the jaw is well tied and healed. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their proper positions, then fevers and usual pains arise, and perhaps dissolution of the belly, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is lost; 
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times they died in nine days. 
de la forcelle	Of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forcele cannot dislocate from within the continuation of it and the foot, and it is dislocated sometimes outwards, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the place with your palm, and it will return; 
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	Then put on the plaster and bandage it, and remove it. 
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	And the head which is towards the elbow cannot dislocate. 
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	If it does, and if it dislocates even once, then reset it in its place, as we have said;  
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put on the plaster and bandage it, and remove it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed. 
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way reset the head of the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.  
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is only dislocated according to three ways: 
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is that it dislocates to the part of the armpit below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is to the part of the buttock; 
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance it dislocates to the part above, and this rarely happens.  
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and do not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate within for the nerves; 
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times dislocate below towards the armpit, similarly for those who have a bone protrusion, because it must be hastened. 
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	For those who have enough flesh, it enters with difficulty and returns with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it sometimes happens to some men that they suffer a blow or fracture, and their shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe it is dislocated because of it.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore, you must test it until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it falls towards the armpit and puts a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find manifest diversity between them. 
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and below the armpit towards the chest, the head of the shoulder as if it were a bone.  
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its place, nor move it in any way. 
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated at the top, unless it is hidden, for you will find it clearly when touching. 
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset, when it is new, or if the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	The method is that the practitioner lifts the patient's hand upward, then puts their fingers under the armpit, and lifts the joint forcefully upward to its place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And the practitioner lifts the hand and extends it upward, then puts it below. 
si venra hastanment.	It will come quickly.  
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said within three days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; 
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and let the patient use a soothing and softening poultice, such as a decoction of marshmallow and fenugreek and melilot in water, and it should be applied. 
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then let the patient be laid on their back, and put a cloth of wool under the armpit, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the patient's heel upon the cloth, and gently lift the head of the shoulder, and pull the hand of the patient; 
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another assistant hold the patient's head so that it does not move down;  
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder will now return to its place, and if you see the resetting according to this method: 
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is for you to have a man who is larger than the patient present;  
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and let him stand straight beside the patient and put his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs on the arm; 
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And another minister pulls the patient's hand towards their belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then you can put something heavy on him, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And we reset it in another way: 
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And one sticks a long coal in the ground, whose head is as round as a pistol, and is neither too thick nor too thin; 
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	Then it is placed under the patient, but with several cloths on top of it, and the patient lies along the length of the wood; 
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then their hand is extended in the opposite direction, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	And if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: 
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a coal two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a round head to enter perfectly under the armpit, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then lay upon the head of the wound cloths underneath so that it does not stain the patient and then put it under the armpit of the patient 
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	And extend his arms upon the length of the wound and bind the shoulder upon the wound and the arm at the head of the hand then put the arm upon the rung of a ladder that is wide and let the hands be extended downwards and let the body hang down on the other side 
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint will come back together now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how, you must put under the shoulder a sphere of wool equal in size; then apply a plaster prepared with powder from the mill, frankincense and egg yolk, over the whole shoulder and bind it; then bind it under the shoulder firmly, and tie the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is fitting that he rest a little while, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly 
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then rest more afterwards for five or seven days and move it.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And if it is firm and not softened, it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced out of place by moisture or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauteries to three holes, as it is shown in front of this chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all of this and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold and cannot raise his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened. 
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And know that the joint is never fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	Dislocation which is towards the shoulder blades, or breasts, or behind, is done by impulse and extension of the hands, and it is administered elsewhere; 
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cure as long as he is healthy. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and slowness in movement, then have the patient bathe many times, until the stiffness is relieved, and it returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of dislocation one must
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated at points and at points it returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and if it is dislocated in all parts, and even in front and behind, the dislocation is not rejoined, for one sees it well and feels it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And it is dislocated according to each shape. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick knife with the healthy one, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is raised, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it behooves you to reset it as abscesses come for if abscesses should come, it would be a hardship to reset it; 
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be completely reset, even when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	If it is worse than other dislocations, and there is greater pain, and perhaps death comes. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such that when it can be brought back, you extend your hand with both hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and your arms are spread, and the hands from above according to the way it was twisted, then and below, push the joint at its edges together, or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand onto his hand, and pulls from the root of the palm or the costal bone which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and have two assistants extend the arm, and hold it so that it does not move during the extension; 
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm from each side, once you have wrapped a long and wide doubled cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the assistants join the joint to your hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in place, put a dry plaster on it with egg yolk, and bandage it firmly, and bind the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for several days, then unbind it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; 
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not holding well, start the plaster and bandage again, and leave it like that for several days, until it is firmly in place; 
puis le deslie.	then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, bathe it and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; 
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or put a greasy sheep's wool on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and put it in a bath; 
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	And when he sweats, if he rubs the joint moderately, then puts the bandage back on, and then goes into a bath; 
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And thus does it twice or three times, until it is healed; 
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	And if you see, put cow dung moistened and heated with butter on top of it;  
si revenra a sa disposition.	It will return to its proper position. 
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is lighter than the other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the flesh does not swell or an abscess becomes hot. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is such that you place the afflicted hand on a table and extend the fingers of the hand, and look at it and put it equally so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns. 
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Nevertheless, it is necessary that you look to see if it is well in place. 
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient's back of his hand on a table at extension and flexion. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, place the patient's back of their hand on the table and the surgeon puts their hand upon that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is good. 
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	But if not, if you bind soothing poultices for abscesses on it, and leave it thus without moving. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in place after several days, the joint remains crooked. 
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	And do not harm the patient further than that while the hand is weakened and cannot grasp anything at all.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery. 
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other remedy than to burn it with a cautery, and perhaps nothing else will do.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and leave it for five days, then untie it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then apply warm water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the wrists of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or in the belly. 
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then stretch the fingers and push the dislocation back into place as far as it will go. Then support the head of the finger and bend it towards the side where it is dislocated 
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then set it equal that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	And from that time on, as we have said, untie it during the day and make it move, and rebind it at night; 
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this often until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same when it is dislocated on another side. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	For the dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	The signs are that the movements jump without volition and it cannot be held, and many times some limb is softened, whether the two thighs or the two arms or one. 
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often it moves the shinbone in four parts; 
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	The one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez": 
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure is that you consider if the gilbositez came from childhood: 
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If there is no cure or healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And the one that comes from falling or impact or similar things, the old ways of cure said in many words, where there is not much profit in all; 
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gilbositez that comes at the front of the foot, there is neither remedy nor healing; 
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight on both sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I say.  
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and let the patient lie on his back in an even place, and have a stretcher beneath him so that he does not get bruised. 
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then put one tongs in the ground at the head and the other at the feet, and tie a cord under the patient's buttocks, and another at the thighs, and at the knees, and at the ankles. 
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	And let two ministers hold the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two tongs.  
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And let them be well fastened, the tongs as we have said, and the surgeon put his palms on the spine straight, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, then take a board three arm-lengths long and wedge it under the wall, and let the patient lie on his side, and put the head of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine.  
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the patient's feet on the other end of the table and press firmly until it returns to its place. 
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you see that it turns in the hand, do it at the elbow. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And put two hot coals on the head of the patient's arm one large and two others towards the feet, and have between each coal, above and below, a palm's length of space. 
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	And have in each coal one hole where the elbow goes and let the coals be firmly in the ground so that they do not move. 
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between each two coals have one turning coal so that the limbs turn and have in the two turnings two small coals a palm's length long to turn the elbow.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.
