And then tie the strap which is among the splints to the elbow towards the head and the other strap towards the feet to the other elbow and each of the assistants turns his elbow at all the straps and the master puts the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are equal, put a drying plaster on them with plenty of egg, and then bandages, and then the splint of a tablet three finger-lengths long, which should cover the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine that is healthy, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use subtle nourishment for the patient until they are healed. 
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if anything comes at the end of health, it is fitting to administer softening and soothing remedies with the splint that we have mentioned before. 
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes one administers a piece of plumb, and sometimes the appearance comes at the back of the spine of the back, and one thinks that it is a dislocation. 
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And it is the bone that appears, for which one should not have presumption.
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Perhaps death would follow. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come out of place as dislocations, and not as other joints do. 
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	And the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:  
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inward and outward, and front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more often inward than outward, and seldom dislocated front and back. 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of this inward dislocation is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee towards the fire. 
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And there is a warmth that comes from a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh bone has come loose there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who is about to die, it is so that this event is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of one who has it beforehand, if it is well aligned according to its completion; 
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Nevertheless, do not bend the knee twice without pain, and if one wants to make it walk, it cannot beforehand, and it retains its urine, and swells the ankle, and when it walks, it passes on the heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has it behind are that he cannot spread his knee nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The resetting of this type of dislocation is such that you consider whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its arrangement, if there is no cure; 
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it should not be presumed. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four types of dislocations, hurry to return the joint, extend it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; 
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	perhaps it will return, and does not need another cure. 
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary that you prepare a strong assistant, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or with a tie that is tied above the knee; 
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And another assistant extends his hand over it in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then you bind him tightly with a soft tie above the thigh; 
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another holds the head of the tie;  
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and you extend upward and downward all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation returns as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this does not work, it is necessary to put a cure in its place. 
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the thighbone, it is necessary that you place the patient on their sound side, then put the tie at the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the groin, then extend the tie upwards towards the groin, and towards the kneecap; 
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take another minister to grasp his arms, and embrace the thick part of the thigh of the sick man, and extend it in a straight form. 
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	It will now return to its place. 
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	And this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, it is fitting that you bind the two feet of the sick man together with a strong tie above the two heels and above the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two parts more than the others.  
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then it should be hung on the top of a beam, and be raised two arm's lengths above the ground; 
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command another minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the sick man who embraces straight the thigh, for the joint now returns quickly.  
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is to the exterior, lay the patient down as we said for those with gout, and tighten the bandage properly on the diseased leg and on the foot too. 
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two embers, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one ember between the patient's thighs in the shape of a letter M. 
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And place cloths dampened with water around it so that it does not burn the patient, then extend each limb towards them and the practitioner places their hand equal to the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a table, and press it down as we have said in the setting of the fracture, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg quickly and according to what I have said. 
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place the practitioner's hand on the diseased angle, then press with the other hand and extend it downwards towards the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is not right to stretch the patient out or lift him up from the ground, but he should be as though his hip were dislocated in the shoulder, as we have said about childbirth on the two hips. 
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And he should be face down, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table. 
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	And it will be done when the patient extends his legs, and they will be equal. 
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	Then adjust the thighs, and apply a plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move. 
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	And he should rest for three or four days, then untie it, and apply the plaster again.
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	And if you see that they are equal, bind it as before, and leave it for three days.
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Then untie it, and make it move gently, until the limb is comforted. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated according to three manners: 
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inwards and outwards, and backwards; 
et ne desalue point devant.	and it does not dislocate forwards. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are such that you order the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not bend at his thigh, know that it is dislocated; 
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all these is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and place his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and draw it back between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee so that they form
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another attendant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that he bends his leg at his thigh easily; 
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on it, and let the leg air out at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three days or four, then unbind it. 
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And let the patient not work at all, until the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all aligned, then apply strong extension as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes loosened, and sometimes completely dislocated, both within and without.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tense before the part where it is dislocated: 
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The setting back should be light, and one should gently extend the hand to its fingers when it is only slightly displaced. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated altogether, it befits you to make the patient sit upright, and hold them firmly by the leg, above the ankle; 
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then draw the foot to you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards, and thrust the foot upwards beautifully; 
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; 
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, it is good; 
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, start the work again, for it will return; 
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return this way, have the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix a stick firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around, so that he does not bruise the patient; 
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot with his hands or a ligature, which he ties around the ankle; 
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then have each assistant extend equally, and let the stick be now between the patient's thighs to hold him down when he is stretched; 
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then place the mirrors equally at the dislocation with his hands, and have another assistant hold the healthy leg underneath, and the dislocation will quickly return. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is set in place, apply a plaster and bandages on top, and bind them tight, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandages are not too tight. 
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, rebind them; 
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; 
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he walks before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is fitting that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it heals.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they can be nicely extended without effort, it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any bone of the back or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table straight, and place your foot on what appears of these joints, then press down firmly with your foot until it returns; 
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is equal, and there is nothing visible, one places under the sole of the foot a board with two legs, then they bind it tight, and leave it for three days, then unbind it. 
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it rest until it is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound accompanies the dislocation and one wishes to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: 
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	do not be presumptuous in the cure if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, do not dare; 
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and at the beginning use soothing things to draw out the abscess, and leave the patient in the hand of God if you do not see hope of recovery; 
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, now reset the limb in its place so that the abscess may drain.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things to the abscess that is hot, and treat the wound as it should be, with drying ointments; 
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if the dislocation is with a fracture, and small bones are broken off, the surgeon must do as we have said in simple diseases; 
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and guard yourself from entering the way of fear, as I have said, for this is worth more according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body.
